**melting like ice**, **vast like tides rising**.

This is not like before,
when it was **vague as if with awareness**,
**indistinct as if without knowledge**—
unnameable.
This **true essence** is indeed the **true One Essence**,
not the **Later-Heaven**’s **intercourse-generated essence**—
it cannot be compared.
It is also the **original essence** of Heaven, Earth, humanity, and all things—
the **common true essence** from which all arise.

Like the **yang at Winter Solstice**,
or the **child at midnight**—
the **achievement of a year in one day**,
though not limited to this,
the **qi mechanism** must all begin here.
Just as the **thousand-layered terrace** begins with **piling earth**,
or the **ten-thousand-li journey** begins with **the first step**—
this is the **root of Heaven, Earth, and humanity’s** **eternal generation**.
If the **root differs**, the **endless branches**—
what limits are there?

Hence, from ancient times to now,
all who cultivate the Dao
never depart from this **gathering of true qi**—
only then does the **symbol of generation** appear.
All things in their **initial arising**,
share this **one true essence**—
forming **symbols** and **bodies**.
How do I know all things share this essence?
**By this:**
Within the **void orifice**,
the **true qi** accumulates—
with time, the **Mysterious Pass opens**,
and the **true essence** is born.

In essence,
**vague** is the **dense radiance**,
**indistinct** is the **subtle mechanism**.
The **Primordial yin** within—
this is the **substance** of **vague and indistinct**.

「坎中真阳，是为杳冥中之精。
Within the **Kan abyss**, the **true yang**—this is the **elusive and profound essence**.

学者必知之真，而后行之至也。
One must first know the **true**,
then practice it to its utmost.

此恍兮惚是性光发越，故云“有象”；
This **vague** and **indistinct**—
its **innate luminous virtue** ascends beyond,
thus it is said to have **"symbols"**.

惚兮恍是以性光下照坎宫，而真阳发动，故云“有物”。
This **indistinct** and **vague**—
its **innate luminous virtue** descends to illuminate the **Kan Palace**,
and the **true yang** stirs into motion,
thus it is said to have **"bodies"**.

窈冥之精，乃二五之精，故云甚真。
The **elusive and profound essence**—
this is the **Five Phases’ true essence**,
thus it is called **most true**.

欲得真精，须知真信。
To obtain the **true essence**,
one must first grasp **true faith**.

真信者，阴阳迭运，不失其候之调，俟其信之初至，的当不易，即行擒伏之功得矣。
**True faith**—
when **yin** and **yang** alternate in their courses,
one does not fail to observe their proper **signs and rhythms**.
Awaiting the **true essence**’s first arrival,
seize it firmly without hesitation,
and the **capturing and subduing** practice is achieved.

凡人修炼之初，必要恍惚杳冥，而后人欲净尽，天理常存，凡息自停，真息乃见。
At the outset of cultivation,
all must pass through **vague and indistinct, elusive and profound**—
then the **human desires** are purified and exhausted,
while **Heavenly principle** remains constant.
The **ordinary breaths** cease naturally,
and the **true breath** emerges.

此何以故？
Why is this so?

盖人心太明，知觉易生。
It is because the **human heart** is too bright,
and **awareness** arises easily.

若到杳冥，知觉不起，即元性元命，打成一片。
Yet when one reaches **elusive and profound**,
**awareness** does not stir—
then **original nature** and **original life** merge as one.

此个恍惚杳冥，大为修士之要。
This **vague and indistinct, elusive and profound**—
it is the **most vital** for the cultivator.

学人当静定之时，忽然偶生知觉，此时神气凝聚丹田，浑然精然，自亦不知其所之，此性命返还于无极之天也。
When the **student** sits in **stillness and calm**,
suddenly **awareness** arises,
at which point **spirit-qi** condenses in the **Elixir Field**,
pure and undivided—
one does not even know where it goes.
This is when **nature and life** return to the **limitless Heaven**.

虽然外有是理，而丹田中必有融和气机，方为实据。
Though externally this **principle** exists,
within the **Elixir Field**, there must be **harmonized qi-machinery**,
only then is it **true foundation**.

由此一点融和，采之归炉，封固温养，自能发为真阳一气。
From this **single point of harmonization**,
gather it and return it to the **Furnace**,
seal it firmly and nurture it warmly—
it will naturally **emanate as true yang qi**.

但行功到此，大有危险。
Yet when one’s practice reaches this point,
**great danger** looms.

惟有一心内守，了照当中，方能团结为丹药，可以长生不老。
Only by **single-heartedly guarding internally**,
and **illuminatingly penetrating the center**,
can one **congeal it into elixir**, achieving **longevity and immortality**.

若生一它念，此个元气，即已杂后天而不纯矣。
If one **harbors another thought**,
this **original qi** will be **mingled with postnatal influences** and become impure.

若动一淫思，此个气机即驰于外，而真精从此泄漏矣。
If one **stirs even one lustful thought**,
this **qi-machinery** will **bolt outward**,
and the **true essence** will **leak away** from here.

古人云：泄精一事，不必夫妻交媾，即此一念之动，真精已不守舍，如走丹一般。
The ancients said:
**"Leaking essence"**—
it need not involve **husband-wife copulation**;
even the stir of **one thought**,
and the **true essence** no longer **resides in its home**,
like **fugitive cinnabar** in flight.

学人必心与气合，息与神交，常在此腔子里，久之，自有无穷趣味生来。
The **student** must **unite heart and qi**,
**intermingle breath and spirit**,
ever abiding in this **chamber**—
with time, **endless joys** will naturally arise.

然而真难事也；
Yet truly, this is **no easy matter**.

设能识透玄机，亦无难事。」
If one can **penetrate and discern the profound mechanism**,
then there is **no difficulty**.

At first, one merely employs the method of **lifting and gathering**—
this **true qi** must not **bolt downward**,
nor must it **scatter through the six orifices**.
It is all about **one-heartedly returning to the command**,
**five-bodied sincerity**.

With time, the **essence will naturally fill**—
no longer craving **color**.

I wish the **student** would **preserve the original essence**,
**not allowing even a drop to leak**.

At first, **constant practice along the familiar Dao** seems difficult;
but if one **endures again and again**,
**not permitting even a thought to stir**,
within **three months**, the **external yang will naturally withdraw**.

When the **external yang is withdrawn**,
then one perceives the **original qi** within the body **abundant**—
and thus the **immortal, ageless sage** is attained.
What is **sagehood**, if it is so distant?

**Chapter Twenty-Two: "Complete and Return"**
*"Crooked, yet whole;
Bent, yet straight;
Hollow, yet full;
Worn, yet renewed;
Few, yet gain;
Many, yet confused."*

Thus the **Sage** embraces **Oneness** as the model for the world.
Not seeing oneself, yet **clear**;
Not asserting oneself, yet **illuminated**;
Not boasting of oneself, yet **accomplished**;
Not vaunting oneself, yet **enduring**.

Only because one **does not contend**,
the world cannot contend with them.

What the ancients called **"crooked, yet whole"**—
was it empty speech?
**Truly, it is complete and returned.**

The **essence of the Great Dao** must **reach the void while containing the full**;
**reverse the full to realize the void**—
only then is it the **Dao of dual cultivation of nature and life**.

For **nature is originally void**—
void arising from the full;
**life is truly full**—
full arising from the void.

If one **fixes on emptiness**, it becomes **stubborn voidness**;
if one **fixes on the full**, it becomes **entangled in names and forms**.
Even if it does not **degenerate into absurd, unorthodox claims**,
it is still **one-sided learning**—
in the end, it cannot equal the **Great Dao**.

The **practitioner** must first **lay down all entanglements**,
**free from even a speck of dust**,
and within **absolute nothingness**,
**seek out a spark of vitality** to serve as the **elixir’s foundation**.
The ancients called this **true yang**,
or **true lead**,
or **the true One-qi**.

The **Taoist Canon** says *"crooked, yet whole"*—
meaning within the **hidden recesses of the body**,
in the **solitary knowing and solitary awareness**,
there exists a **wholly undivided, lively, and flowing mechanism**.
By **nurturing and refining** this,
one can attain **elixir completion and sagehood**.

The ancients likened it to the **slightest line of yang at Winter Solstice**,
which **generates endlessly**.
Or the **slim crescent of the new moon on the third day**,
gradually waxing to the **full moon on the fifteenth**—
all are expressions of **"crooked, yet whole."**

For **crooked is hidden**—
in the **subtle depths**, its **mechanism is subtle**,
yet its **fulfillment is vast**.
As the *Zhongyong* says: *"Crooked can possess"*—
truly so.

Within this **single crook**,
there is nothing but the **origin of principle and qi**;
within this **whole body**,
it is the **essence of the Great Ultimate**—
thus, *"crooked, yet whole."*

The **Sage** found this crook,
**diligently and cautiously**,
**cycling and embracing**, like a hen brooding,
like a dragon guarding its pearl—
**one-heartedly guarding within**, not allowing it to **leak outward**.

With time, it **swells like the tide**,
**rising and stretching upward**,
a **single current of clear, rigid qi**,
**boldly ascending** beyond sun and moon,
**encompassing** heaven and earth.

The *Kun* hexagram says:
*"Kun is supremely yielding, yet in movement, it is rigid"*—
all from the **aftermath of bending**,
**hidden in the earthen vessel**,
**accumulating until it overflows the heavens**,
**bursting forth uncontrollably**—
such is its nature.

Moreover, **bent becomes yin, becomes yielding**—
this is the same qi;
**straight becomes yang, becomes rigid**—
also this same qi.
Though it is said *"from bent to straight"*, in truth,
**it is both bent and straight**.

After **piercing the source from within the hidden crook**,
its **manifestation becomes easy**,
but **guarding it is difficult**.

Only by **resting in ease, drifting in play**,
**nurturing its subtle traces**,
**lowering oneself to serve others**,
**humbling oneself in self-regard**,
can one **avoid the nature of haste and violence**,
**not generate deluded views**,
**not stir the vulgar fire**—
only then can **golden elixir** be formed.

Thus, **spirit governs qi**,
**qi unites with spirit**,
**hidden and revealed without trace**,
**transformation beyond measure**—
**"utter sincerity without pause**,
**embodying things without omission**,
**present everywhere yet nowhere"**—
how **full** it is!

Yet one must **be humble to receive benefit**,
**hollow to become full**.
Otherwise, how could one **embrace all things**?

Much less this **subtle crook**—
all originally **our own substance**—
what is called **"worn"**—
**worn is the old**.

As the *Zhongyong* says: *"Temper the old to know the new."*
The **student** who seeks **new growth to generate new ideas**,
if not by **nurturing this old substance**,
how could they **know the new**?
This is also **"worn, yet renewed."**

Though **wornness is scarce**,
if one **nurtures it from its fewness**,
the **vast qi** can **fill heaven and earth**, **pierce the Horns of the Bull**.
If one claims the **Dao is vast, encompassing all**,
and **takes from its abundance**,
I fear **desire and principle will be mixed**,
**good and evil indistinguishable**—
sometimes **holding to the middle**,
sometimes **gathering herbs**,
sometimes **advancing fire, withdrawing talismans**,
**fixating on forms, grasping names**—
the more, the better—
yet it remains **rootless learning**,
**unable to return to stillness**,
ultimately a **tangled knot**.

No wonder one **spends a lifetime in doubt, yet never awakens**.

The **Sage** cultivates **Oneness** for themselves,
and applies it to the world,
as a **model for all**.
If one does not know that the **Dao of the crook** is truly the **unifying Dao**,
and **occasionally strays**—
**once strayed, there is no model**,
**no model, no attainment**—
what reliance is there on the **Dao**?

The **Dao is originally the unified principle of heaven and humanity**,
**all things and self**—
a **common substance**.
Yet today’s scholars **each cling to their own views**,
claiming none surpass them—
this **arrogant pride** alone
already **obscures the luminous clarity**,
while they fail to **measure the ancient against the present**,
**take the superior as their standard**.

The *Zhongyong* says:
*"The Dao of the **Noble** shines **dimly yet clearly**;
the Dao of the **petty** shines **brightly yet perishes."*

「Indeed, the **Dao of the sincere cultivator** is something to be held with **solemn reverence**. Even if one approaches the **transformation into the divine** (*shénhuà*),
it is merely what one ought to do and what one ought to fulfill—
why must one **boast to the world** and **exaggerate one’s merits**?
If one **praises oneself**,
not only will one be **despised by others**,
but the **merits themselves will be false and not true**.

The ancients, having attained their **merits**, withdrew humbly—
they **never claimed credit** for their deeds,
**truly covering the world with their virtue** and becoming **teachers for all ages**.
As for **self-cultivation and self-forging** (*zìxiū zìliàn*),
it is like **clothing that brings warmth** or **food that satiates hunger**—
all are **self-acquired joys**,
and yet, they are **what others also possess and find sufficient**.
Why must one **swagger with arrogance** and **pretend to be great**,
**boasting of one’s strengths**?
Though it is said that **wisdom grows daily** and **cleverness expands each day**,
this is merely **what all humans share**—
I have simply **attained it first**;
where is the **true length** of it?

If one **boasts of one’s strengths**,
then one’s **strengths will become weaknesses**.
Even the most **foolish of men**—
who would willingly **lag behind**?
Where do **disputes** not begin from here?
The **Noble** has **no place for contention**,
so the world cannot **contend with their power**.
The ancients spoke of **"crook/turning brings completeness"** (*qǔ zé quán*)—
truly, this is not **empty talk**,
but refers to **one who fully receives and fully returns** the **Dao**?
This is the **unifying Dao** (*Zhōngyōng*), or next, the **Dao of the crook/turning** (*qǔ*), which can **sincerely embody the Dao**.
The **crook/turning** is the **hidden crook** (*yǐnqǔ*), the **Dao** calls it **"mysterious orifice"** (*Xuánqiào*),
the **Buddha** names it **"that"** (*nàge*),
and the **Confucian** refers to it as **"the origin and traces"** (*duānní*).
Yet it is **not empty nor without substance**—
a **single point** from which **all things and beings** arise.

When **heaven and earth opened** (*kāipì*) and **figures began to emerge** (*wùrén shǐshēng*),
all originated from this **one point**,
and its **movement and stillness** are visible at all times.
When it **stays still and begins to manifest**,
it does not arise from **external stimulation**.
Suddenly **awakened**,
this **awakening itself is the crook/turning** (*qǔ*).
When it **moves and displays its form**,
it arises from **spontaneous resonance** (*gǎnfú*).
Suddenly **stirred**,
this **stirring itself is the crook/turning**.

Essentially, it is when one is **in ignorance and unawareness**,
and the **qi-mechanism** (*qìjī*) moves **spontaneously**—
**moving and suddenly awakening**—
this is **true movement and true awakening**.
But its **mechanism is extremely subtle**,
its **timing swiftest**—
a **mere shift in thought** or **change in breath**,
and it already belongs to **postnatal cultivation** (*hòutiān*),
**unable to serve as the root of life** for all things and beings,
**nor as the foundation for refining the elixir** (*liàn dān*).
Humans receive **qi** and form **bodies** (*chéngxíng*),
become **people and things** (*wùrén*),
all from this **single thought** (*yī niàn*) that **branches into myriad forms** (*fēn tāi*).
The **right and wrong paths of cultivation** (*xiédào*),
the **true and false nature of the Dao**—
which does not originate from this **single thought**?

The *Zhōushū* says:
*"**Erroneous thoughts lead to madness** (*wàng niàn zuò kuáng*),
**overcoming thoughts leads to sainthood** (*kè niàn zuò shèng*)."*
The **difference between sainthood and madness** lies in **a single thought**—
so swift, so decisive!
This is what **"crook/turning"** (*qǔ*) truly means.
The ancients likened it to **a flash of lightning or a spark of stone fire** (*diàn guāng shíhuǒ*),
or **a steed galloping a thousand li without leaving dust** (*qiān lǐ jì zú*).
At this moment, one must have **a bright pearl of wisdom** (*zhìzhū lǎngzhào*),
only then can one **recognize it clearly**.

Having **grasped this origin and trace** (*duānní*),
one must still **nurture and expand** it—
as **Mencius** said:
*"Fire just begins to burn*,
*the spring just begins to flow*—
**vast and blazing** (*hào hào yán yán*),
**naturally filling heaven and earth** (*tiān dì*)."*
Yet the **way of nurturing and expansion**—
is there truly another?
If one **does not bend and humble oneself** (*wǎng qū zìchí*),
then one’s **true qi cannot stretch** (*zhèngqì bù néng chángshēn*).
If one **does not lower and abase oneself** (*bēi wā zìxià*),
then one’s **heavenly virtue cannot be complete** (*tiāndé bù néng chángyuán*).
Only by **guarding the original substance within oneself and all things** (*shǒu wú shēn*),
**not engaging nor separating** (*bù cān bù èr*),
**warming the old** (*wēn qí gù*),
**embracing the one** (*bào yī qí*),
**not seeking novelty in new ends** (*bù qiú zhī yú xīn yīng zhī duān*),
**nor indulging in the proliferation of names and forms** (*bù chǐ zhī yú míng xiàng zhī fán*),
can one **avoid becoming more confused with each day of learning**,
and instead **find joy in the ceaseless renewal** (*rìxīn yòu xīn*).

The **ancient sages** knew that the **crook/turning** (*qǔ*) is the **stage for attaining immortality and sainthood** (*chéngxiān zhèngshèng*),
so they **embraced the divine and relied on qi** (*shén bào qì*),
**qi followed the divine and divine-qi merged as one without separation** (*qì yī shén, shén qì hé yī bù lí*),
as the **essence of self-cultivation** (*zìxiū zhī yào*),
and as the **model for all under heaven** (*tiānxià zhī shì*).
If one **only sees oneself and insists on one’s own views** (*zì jiàn zì shì*),
then one **obscures the luminous clarity** (*mèi qí míng ér bù zhāng*),
let alone **praises oneself and claims credit** (*zì fǎ ér bù zhēn*),
**boasts of strengths and ignores weaknesses** (*zì jīn ér duǎn ér bù cháng*).
**Wisdom arising from emotions** (*zhì qǐ qíng shēng*)
often **becomes the Dao’s greatest harm**.
Only by **not seeing oneself nor insisting on one’s own views**,
**not praising oneself nor boasting of strengths**,
can one’s **mind be level and qi harmonious** (*xīn píng qì hé*),
**naturally avoiding evil in others** (*bìmǐ wū è*),
**and corruption in oneself** (*cǐlǐ wú cuì*),
so who could **contend with them**?

The **Dao’s subtle and silent influence** (*qián yí mòqì*) is such—
unless one **embraces the one** (*bào yī*) and **fully receives and fully returns** the **Dao** (*quán shòu quán guī*),
how can one **return to the primal origin** (*fǎn qí tàishǐ zhī chū*)?

**Chapter 23: Rare Words, Naturalness**
Rare words, naturalness.
Thus, **gusts of wind do not last all morning**,
**sudden rains do not last all day**.
Who is responsible for this?
**Heaven and earth**.
Even **heaven and earth cannot endure long**,
let alone **humans**?
Therefore, those who **pursue the Dao**:
—**those who align with the Dao** (*tóng yú dào zhě*) are **in harmony with the Dao** (*dào yě lè dé zhī*),
—**those who align with virtue** (*tóng yú dé zhě*) are **in harmony with virtue** (*dé yě lè dé zhī*),
—**those who align with loss** (*tóng yú shī zhě*) are **in harmony with loss** (*shī yě lè dé zhī*).
**Truly, there is no joy in being unaligned** (*xìn bùzú yān, yǒu bùxìn yān*).
The **Dao originally has no sound nor breath** (*wú shēng wú xī*),
so it is called **"rare words"** (*xī yán*).
The **Dao originally has no action nor doing** (*wú wéi wú zuò*),
so it is called **"naturalness"** (*zìrán*).

What **things can endure** and **affairs can last**?
None but those that **follow heaven’s movement** (*shùn tiān ér dòng*),
**act in accordance with their nature** (*shuài xìng yǐ xíng*),
and **listen to the qi-mechanism’s spontaneous operation** (*yī tīng qìjī zhī zìyùn*).
If one **forces and contrives** (*jiǎo niǔ zào zuò*),
**unable to follow the qi-mechanism** (*bù néng shùn qí jī*),
and **cannot conform to the revolutions of heaven and earth** (*hé yīn qián kūn zhī yùn zhuǎn*),
the **rising and setting of the sun and moon** (*rìyuè zhī shēng héng*),
then one’s **efforts will be like fleeting winds over boiling water** (*piāo táng zhī fēng*),
**violent rains** (*kuáng bào zhī yǔ*),
**uprooting great trees** (*bó dà mù*),
**flooding flat plains** (*yǒng píng chuān*),
**coming swiftly and departing swiftly**—
their **force could not possibly last all day or all morning**!

Yet who is responsible for this?
Ask **heaven and earth**, and they **do not know**.
**Heaven and earth** are the **masters of all things** (*wànwù zhī zhǔzǎi*),
yet even they **cannot endure long** if they **do not follow their natural ways** (*bù shùn qí cháng*).
How much more so for **humans**, who are **like a single grain in the great granary** (*tài cāng yī sù*)?
Who could **endure long** by **not following the Dao of constancy**?

Thus, the **Greatest Sage** (*Tàishàng*) spoke of the **source of the Dao**,
**taking non-action as its core** (*wúwéi wéi zōng*),
and **naturalness as its application** (*zìrán wéi yòng*).
If one **does not pursue this**,
but instead **boasts of shortcuts** (*qiā kuài jìng*),
**seeks out divine wonders** (*lìng xù shénqí*),
one is **misguided**!
Look at those who **pursue the Dao**—
though they may be **far apart in the four directions** (*dōng xī nán běi zhī yáo*),
and their **teachings differ** (*shēngjiào gè yì*),
yet if they **have a resolve for the Dao** (*yǒu zhì yú dào*),
and **do not stray into false paths** (*bù rù xiétú*),
they **all converge seamlessly without gap**.

To walk the Dao and gain insight in one’s heart is called **virtue** (*dé*).
Once one knows how to cultivate the Dao,
**virtue** naturally arises within.
All who clearly manifest their **virtue**,
free from distraction and strife,
find themselves in silent accord as one.

Thus it is said:
*"Those who align with the Dao are one with the Dao,
those who align with **virtue** are one with **virtue**—
what wonder is there in this?"*

At the outset of practice,
cultivation follows **Dao** and **virtue**,
tracks and norms are observed,
effortless and unburdened, free from entanglement.
When one reaches the stage of profound self-realization,
settled in ease and depth,
resources flow effortlessly in all directions—
what was once gained now seems lost,
as pure effort fuses into oneness,
like crafting a wheel behind closed doors,
only to find it fit perfectly upon emergence—
all is unified.

Thus it is said:
*"Those who lose are one with loss."*

These three stages reflect differing levels of attainment,
each progressing along distinct paths.
Yet with prolonged effort and endurance through hardship,
even suffering transforms into serene ease,
abundant with delight—
spontaneously, one’s true nature unfolds.
When suffering is exhausted, what joy knows bounds!
Thus it is said:
*"Those who align with the Dao find the Dao delights in them;
those who align with **virtue** find **virtue** delights in them;
those who align with loss find loss delights in them."*

For the essence of **non-action** is what all may cultivate,
and the art of **naturalness** is what all may employ.
Even sages of ten thousand *li* or gods of ten thousand years—
though time and place may shift—
naturally converge as if seals fitting together,
all returning to the same path.

If one claims **naturalness** is not thus,
then bias clouds the mind,
and divergent methods arise within.
Some cling rigidly to the concrete, stubbornly fixed,
others cling to emptiness, practicing solitary stillness.
Such cases are countless—
all stem from failing to trust the principle of **non-action**,
the Dao of **naturalness**,
and instead clinging to their own views as truth.

No wonder those who begin young in the Dao
find no fruition in their later years—
their resolve outstrips their learning,
and they spend their lives never grasping the true meaning,
straying into false paths.
How tragic!
How lamentable!

This speaks of the **Dao of non-action and naturalness**—
the same that governs heaven and earth, sun and moon,
the unseen and the spirits of the dead.
All follow this principle:
non-action and naturalness,
letting birth unfold as it will,
serving their purpose and acting as they must.

Yet ordinary people, once born,
exhaust their wit and cunning day and night—
how much of their innate nature remains intact?
Only those of lofty **Dao** follow nature’s constant way.

Though their early efforts may require striving,
once perfected, they return to the realm of non-action and naturalness—
effortless, as if attained without thought,
achieved without strain,
moving naturally along the **Way**.

Thus, when sages observe the Great **Dao**,
its principle of non-action and naturalness
shines clearly before all eyes,
unspoken yet universally understood.
But for later generations viewing the Great **Dao**,
its attainment seems reserved only for sages and immortals—
common folk dare not speak of it.

*The Zhongyong* says:
*"Strive in learning, struggle in effort—
success brings unity."*
Is this mere deceit?
No.

The origin lies in a heart that initially lacks faith,
entering through the path of **non-Dao**,
and as time progresses, it grows ever more distant and estranged—
thus, the **Way** of non-action and naturalness
cannot be fully shared,
and distinctions arise, dividing as if into separate households.
Those who study must understand this,
lest they be misled by peripheral **Dao** and false paths.

**Chapter Twenty-Four**
*Those who stand on tiptoe cannot stand,*
*those who stride cannot walk;*
*those who seek self-visibility remain blind,*
*those who insist on self-righteousness fail to shine;*
*those who boast of their own merits gain no true achievement,*
*those who vaunt their own virtues do not endure.*
In regard to the **Way**,
they are but gluttonous excess and burdensome exertion.
Since others may detest this,
those who truly follow the **Way** do not dwell upon it.

Earlier, it was said that the **Way** is rare in its naturalness—
not like the world’s coarse and dull masses,
who mistake recklessness for non-action,
and abandon for naturalness.
Yet, its essence is the Great **Dao** of perfect balance,
conforming to Heaven’s principle and human nature,
following the sages’ **virtue** and the sovereign’s **Way**,
preserving and reflecting inward,
returning to the root and restoring the origin—
thus, aligning above with Heaven’s decree,
it achieves non-action yet nothing remains undone,
and naturalness without deviation.
The *Yijing* says:
*"Exhaust the principles, fulfill innate nature,
and reach the realm of fate."*
Is this not the ideal?

Excess is a disease,
and insufficiency is also a disease.
The *Shujing* states:
*"Without bias or faction,
the sovereign’s **Way** flows vast and unrestricted."*
This is exactly so.

Even in human posture,
there exists an unchanging norm.
*Standing on tiptoe* means two feet propped up—
as the *Shijing* says:
*"I stand on tiptoe, gazing at you,"*
using this posture to observe others allows one to survey the horizon,
but if one seeks to stand long,
how can it be sustained?
*Striding* means two feet stretched wide—
to mount a horse, one may rest upon the saddle,
but if one wishes to walk,
how can it be done?
The enlightened do not insist on self-righteousness;
self-righteousness blinds them.
Those who shine do not seek self-visibility;
self-visibility obscures their brilliance.
Those who boast of their own merits often achieve nothing,
while those with true merit cannot be concealed—
why boast at all?
Those who vaunt their own virtues often lack endurance,
while those with genuine virtue command natural reverence—
why pride oneself?

If one does not believe in the **Way** of non-action and naturalness,
and does not know the principle of *"without doing yet done,"*
*"without striving yet achieved,"*
where all action is entrusted to Heaven,
how free and boundless it is!
To move is to move without resistance,
to halt is to halt without strain—
movement and stillness blend in effortless spontaneity,
how tranquil and serene!

If one fails to grasp the **Way** of emptiness without trace,
it is akin to greatness yet unable to contain—
or if one adds a single intention,
or forces a single perception,
like a glutton’s overindulgence,
or a traveler’s excessive labor—
not only is it unbeneficial,
but it also brings harm.
Those who study must follow the **virtue/power** of Heaven without obstruction,
conform to the natural principles of things,
and not merely interject human contrivance—
even the things themselves should be allowed their natural ease.
Adjust their diet and rest,
for even slight imbalance beyond proper measure—
whether overfeeding or excessive asceticism—
like a dog’s overindulgence causing injury,
or an ox’s overwork leading to exhaustion—
this only breeds internal unrest and self-detestation.
Hence it is said:
*"Others may detest this."*

Those who twist and strain,
seeking to stand or walk,
to shine or be renowned,
whose merits stir the world
and virtues surpass the crowd—
how utterly difficult it is!
The virtuous **Way**-follower despises such folly
and deems it unworthy of their own practice.

This rare naturalness is but one thing: **cleanness**.
What is **clean**?
When no thought arises.
What is **pure**?
When not a speck of dust adheres.
The heart must be like a mirror untainted by dust,
like still water unrippled by waves—
a boundless, luminous spirit,
and this is **cleanness and purity**.

Yet if the world’s ordinary men and vulgar folk,
dim-witted and oblivious,
spend their days doing nothing,
it is not **cleanness and purity**.
True **cleanness** holds light,
true **purity** reveals form—
like a clear pool reflecting the moon,
a single radiance of brilliance—
only then does one attain the reality of **cleanness and purity**.
If even a trace of self-visibility or self-righteousness remains,
it becomes an obstruction.
Thus, those who study the **Way** must cultivate a heart vast and unrestrained,
letting no matter or thing disturb their mind,
or occupy their inner sanctum.
Through prolonged nurturing,
a single luminous spark illuminates all—
as if the sun and moon hung in the sky,
penetrating every corner without fail.
Only fear that a moment’s clarity
follows another moment’s unrestrained indulgence—
then clarity will not remain constant.

Mencius’ strength lay in **nurturing qi**,
for when **qi** is undisturbed, the spirit naturally illuminates,
and when the spirit is luminous, the heart finds peace—
thus he did not say *"nurture the heart"* but *"nurture qi,"*
truly understanding that a unified will moves **qi**,
and unified **qi** moves the will.
If one does not seek to **nurture qi**,
but merely claims to *"nurture the heart,"*
how many will fail to find true heart’s repose their entire lives?

If the heart is truly **cleanness and purity**,
the true **Yang** naturally arises.
All ascension and descent, movement and stillness,
must follow their natural course.
To force tiptoeing into standing,
or striding into walking—
gluttonous excess and burdensome exertion—
all are improper.
Even things detest such imbalance,
and how much more so humans?
Thus, the virtuous **Way**-follower
refuses to indulge in it.

**Chapter Twenty-Five**
**The Way Follows Naturalness**
There exists a formless fusion,
born before Heaven and Earth,
silent and boundless,
self-sufficient yet unchanging,
endlessly circulating yet never exhausted—
it may be called the Mother of all under Heaven.

I do not know its name,
so I call it **Way**,
and forcefully name it **Great**.
**Great** means to pass,
to pass means to go far,
to go far means to return.
Thus, the **Way** is **Great**,
Heaven is **Great**,
Earth is **Great**,
and the sovereign is also **Great**.
Within the realm, there are four **Great**s,
and the sovereign stands as one among them.

The sovereign follows Earth,
Earth follows Heaven,
Heaven follows the **Way**,
and the **Way** follows naturalness.
What is the **Way**?
In the time before **Hongmeng** had yet divided,
before Heaven and Earth showed signs,
before beings took form—
a hazy, indistinct **qi**,
a boundless, formless unity.

Boundless and limitless,
Measureless and boundless,
Seems there exists a thing,
From **Hongmeng** (*混沌*) born,
Swirling and taking form,
Before Heaven and Earth arose—
This is what is called **Wuji** (*无极*).

Silent and void yet bearing life’s potential,
Vast and empty yet containing motion’s intent—
This is what is called **Taiji** (*太极*).

All things possess two,
Yet **Taiji** alone has none.
From one movement, Heaven and Earth split,
Yin and Yang divide,
The Four Symbols and Five Phases unfold,
Encompassing all within.

Humans multiply,
Sun and Moon wax full—
Does not life’s abundance drain **Taiji**?
Yet unknown is this **Hongmeng** thing,
Unseen, unheard,
Yet in all things present,
In all times abiding,
Alone yet undivided,
Whole within chaos—
Yet ever generating, ever transforming,
From **Hongmeng** to this day,
Unchanging in its constancy,
Within its independence, one **qi** flows,
Permeating the **Dharmadhatu** (*法界*), opening and closing as it wills,
Endlessly revolving.

To speak of ordinary things,
It seems this **Way** would be exhausted!
Who knows it circulates through the Three Realms (*三界*),
Fills all beings,
Heaven relies on it to remain clear,
Earth on it to stay serene,
The grains on it to flourish,
Humans on it to live—
All follow its natural course.

Within it, what is born is born of itself,
What is formed is formed of itself,
Yet **Taiji** remains whole and complete,
Unchanged by the process.

Though myriad transformations arise without end,
None escape its signs and names,
Thus it may be called the Mother of all under Heaven.

Heaven is most sublime,
And from its sublimity it may be named;
Earth is most vast,
And from its vastness it may be named.
Yet this **Wuji**—the **Wuji** of **Wuji**—
Not divine yet the divine,
Without sound or scent,
Without form or image,
Yet in quiet repose it never ceases.

I do not know its true name,
So I call it **Way** and **Great**.
**Great** then encompasses all,
**Passing** (*逝*) reaches everywhere,
**Far** (*远*) attains the unattainable.
Know that exhaustion brings return,
For the **Way**’s **Greatness**,
It is not merely one among the Four **Great**s!

Those seeking the **Way**’s ultimate truth
Must not merely speak of naturalness,
But focus mind and regulate breath—
Concentrate the mind, and it does not scatter,
Then humanity’s **heart** is upright, as Heaven and Earth’s **heart**;
Adjust the breath, and it does not stray,
Then humanity’s **qi** flows, as Heaven and Earth’s **qi** does too.
To harmonize with **Qiankun** (*乾坤*), to govern Heaven and Earth—
What greater labor is there?
It lies within one mind, one body,
A breath’s length away.

*The Doctrine of the Mean* says:
"Attain **Zhonghe** (*中和*), and Heaven and Earth stand firm,
All beings flourish."
Is this not its meaning?

If one preserves the mind at all times,
Nurtures **qi** in every moment,
Except when eating to dispel hunger
Or sleeping to dispel weariness—
Then in all things, ever-aware,
No thought wandering, no breath faltering,
Only then does one avoid illness.

Otherwise, the slightest negligence brings decay,
External evils seize and disturb.
When **right qi** is lost,
**Evil qi** easily invades—
This is inevitable.

The ancients said:
"If one does not stir a thought,
Does not harbor a desire,
Heaven and Earth cannot peer into one’s secrets,
Ghosts and spirits cannot fathom one’s subtleties—
Truly not false!"

Some say to establish a foundation (*筑基*)
Is the path to longevity.
But for those who practice the **Way**,
No foundation need be built—
So long as mind and **qi** remain ever bound as one,
No scattering allowed,
Then ghosts and spirits cannot chase the soul or seize the spirit,
One’s life is in one’s own hands, not Heaven’s.

The Master says:
*"I do not fear the blame of indiscretion—*
If later scholars fail to uphold this practice as I have taught,
Then they have no means to stand before me.

**Chapter Twenty-Six: Heavy as the Root of Light, Stillness as the Lord of Agitation**
Heavy is the root of light,
Stillness is the sovereign of agitation.
Thus, the Sage moves through the day without straying from the weight of his burden.
Though he enjoys splendor and spectacle,
His spirit remains detached, as in repose.

Alas! How can a ruler of ten thousand chariots
Cast his own body as light upon the world?
Lightness brings loss of **right qi**,
Agitation brings loss of spirit.
The Dao of cultivation concerns but two things—**qi** and spirit;
Refining and nourishing them
Is to return to the pristine Heaven of **Primordial Oneness**.

In **Preheaven** (*先天*), **qi** is undifferentiated, blending into formlessness,
Thick and heavy, ever at rest;
Spirit dwells in the intangible, void yet luminous, beyond description.
Once **Postheaven** (*后天*) is reached,
The heavy **qi** becomes light and disperses,
The still spirit grows agitated and restless.
**Qi** no longer matches the **Preheaven** vitality,
Ever damp and murky, lacking purity;
Spirit no longer mirrors the **Preheaven** clarity,
Severed from its root, shining alone.
Thus, life cannot stand firm,
And nature becomes difficult to refine.

Scholars who seek longevity
Must know that **qi** must return to its root.
How does it return?
The light and scattered **qi** must be restored
To the domain of solidity and depth,
Steadfast as a mountain, condensed as one mass—
Then **qi** returns to life,
And its vastness fills the Heaven.
The restless and wild spirit must be brought back
To the realm of purity and transparency,
Ever lucid, ever at ease—
Then spirit returns to nature,
And the whole becomes boundless and formless.
Thus, when spirit returns to its original nature,
And **qi** returns to its original life,
It is as though Heaven and Earth had not yet emerged,
Boundless and without end.
The more solid and concentrated it is,
The swifter its motion;
The more void and unmarked it is,
The more limitless its use.

From this, the heavier **qi** becomes the lighter—
The so-called **"Grand Qi"** (*浩然之气*), most vast and most firm,
Filling and permeating Heaven and Earth.
This is the spirit that can be still yet also move—
The *Yijing* says: *"Wondrous in all things, it is the spirit."
Indeed, as Confucius’ disciple Zisi said: *"Perfect sincerity is like the spirit."*

Thus, the Sage in the **Way**
Moves through the day without straying from his burden,
For fear that lightness will drain **qi**,
And hinder the flow of his practice.
Such steadfastness does not slow his progress?
Alas! Though there be the beauty of sound and color,
The allure of wealth and gain,
These are the adornments of the common crowd,
Not the concern of the **Way**-bearing noble.
When faced with the present moment,
The noble one remains as detached as in solitude,
Transcending the world’s attractions—
None know he exists.

Yet how can one of such exalted station,
Of supreme honor and worth,
With a body capable of becoming an immortal or Buddha,
Fail to cherish himself,
But instead take worldly glory and human pleasures as his bond?
Is this not to make his body light,
And to regard himself as too small?

Lightness means losing **right qi**—
**Right qi** is the **qi** of the subject—
To lose **right qi** is to lose form and substance.
Agitation means losing spirit—
Spirit is the **sovereign**—
To lose spirit is to lose sovereignty.
When both spirit and **qi** are lost,
How can the body endure?
This is truly to not know
That the human form is rare,
That China’s soil is hard to birth,
Yet to cast oneself as light—
Is this not a cause for deep lament?

Some cling to worldly splendor,
Envy the path of officialdom,
Saying that profit for oneself is abundant,
And that enriching one’s family is flourishing—
Yet they do not see
That the field of wealth and power
Is also the field of blade and strife!
From ancient times, elephants burned by their tusks,
Jade stones ruined by their embrace,
Their harm can be counted in full.
How can people see only the small,
And not heed the great?

Ah! The pain is bitter indeed!

「Water is light and floats—
This is the **postnatal qi** of the Dao,
Belonging to **external medicine**;

Gold is heavy and sinks—
This is the **prenatal essence** of the Way,
Called **true lead**—
Also called **gold elixir**, also called **the White Tiger’s first crescent breath**,
Its names are manifold—
This is **internal medicine**.

The prenatal gold generates water,
As the **natural order** of **sequential cultivation**,
And births humanity through it—
Thus it is said: *"Heavy as the root of light."*

After birth, humanity is purely
The reckless, turbulent, and light-floating **postnatal qi** at work—
Hence water-qi is light and floats,
Giving rise to manifold passions and desires,
The **essence of life** is lost,
And thus aging and decline come easily.

The **worthy** has the **method of inverse cultivation**—
None other than water returning to generate gold,
Light returning to heavy,
To restore the **original unity of Heaven’s breath**.

Thus, throughout the day,
They move without abandoning the **burden of refinement**—
Only to stand firm and upright,
Stable and uniquely established,
Thick and heavy without wavering,
Nurturing **vast qi** to fill the cosmos.

This is the **Dao of inverse cultivation for immortals**,
Where alchemy is practiced.

In sum: from **form** to **formlessness**,
This is but one matter of the **elixir’s Dao**.

Fire is dry and active—
This is the **postnatal spirit** of the Way,
Belonging to **external medicine**;

Wood is still and congealed—
This is the **prenatal original nature** of the Way,
Called **true mercury**, **true essence**,
Also called **the breath of the Azure Dragon**,
**True Unity’s breath**—
Its names are also many—
All are **internal medicine**.

The prenatal wood generates fire,
As the **natural order** of **sequential cultivation**,
And births humanity through it—
Thus it is said: *"Stillness is the sovereign of agitation."*

After the body takes form,
Purely the **spirit of erratic reasoning and delusion** rules—
Hence fire’s nature is wild and unrestrained,
With manifold deceits and transformations,
Its true essence is bound and obscured,
And thus weakness and collapse come easily.

The **worthy** has the **method of inverted application**—
None other than fire returning to generate wood,
Agitation returning to stillness,
To restore the **original unity of the spirit**.

Though there may be splendor and ease,
And dwelling in lofty detachment—
It is but all phenomena emptied,
One true essence held close—
Nurturing the **awakened True Golden Immortal**,
Summoning the **heavenly realms**—
This is the **elixir’s Dao of inverse refinement**,
Whereby immortality is attained.

In essence: from **awareness** to **formlessness**,
This is another branch of **cultivation**.

This is the refinement of **external medicine** to **internal medicine**,
From **postnatal** back to **prenatal**.

Let me further elucidate:
The **Dao of birth** follows the **natural order**,
The **Dao of immortality** inverts and overcomes it—
For without overcoming, there is no birth,
Nor without overcoming can one attain attainment.
Thus the **River Diagram** and **Luo Scripture** employ both **generation** and **overcoming**.

The **Confucian** and **Buddhist** methods of cultivation differ from mine—
They generally follow the **natural order**,
Conforming to the **degree of spontaneity**;

My **Dao** alone inverts and refines,
Requiring **diligent effort** in its practice.
If one fails to overcome,
There is no way to birth or attain.

But to cultivate in accordance with the **natural order** is easy,
While to invert and refine is difficult.
Without a **true master**,
Unclear of the **correct method**,
And recklessly gathering or refining—
Few escape harm.

Once the **true master** is obtained,
And the **correct method** is clear—
If one does not **seize the opportunity for immortality**,
Nor **cultivate the merit of virtue**,
Then **Heaven’s spirit** will not aid,
And **demonic illusions** will entangle—
There will surely be those who nearly attain but fail,
Whose **elixir collapses**, **cauldron tips over**,
And whose **life and essence are both lost**—
This is truly something to be cautious about.

How does one **invert and overcome**?
First, one follows the **natural order**,
Imitating the **method of husband and wife**,
With **fire entering the domain of water**—
This is **spirit entering qi**,
The **common folk’s father and mother** uniting to produce **medicine**.

When fire steams and water boils,
Gold is born from the depths of water—
At this moment, the **mystic orifice opens**,
And **true faith** arrives—
This is the **true yang** birthing,
And the **medicine-child** is produced—
This is **external medicine**.

Once the **golden-qi** is born,
**True lead** is sufficient—
I, with **fire urging water to ascend**,
**Wood bearing gold aloft**,
Urge it gently, guide it carefully,
Lifting it to the **Heavenly Cauldron**,
To pair **true lead** with **true mercury**,
To use **true fire** and **true intent** to draw it,
Lowering it into the **elixir field**,
Entering the **Earth’s womb**—
Refining the **medicine** with the **cauldron and furnace**,
This is **returning to Kan as male**,
And **restoring Li as female**.

Inverting male and female,
Selecting them as **host and guest**,
Drawing them back into the **furnace**,
Refining them for a **morning’s watch**,
Then awaiting the **true yang fire’s movement**,
To form the **great medicinal fire**—
This is the **birth of internal medicine**,
Also called **the great medicine’s production**.

This is the **sage-father and holy-mother** uniting to nurture.

Moreover, the **small medicine’s** birth,
Its movement lies outside the **kidney passage**,
Its **qi** is weak—
Thus it is called **small medicine, external medicine**;

This one’s movement lies within the **qi’s root**,
When born, there are **heavenly response stars**,
**Earthly response tides**,
And the **six senses tremble**—
Thus it is called **internal medicine, great medicine**,
Also called **gold elixir**.

Again, with this **gold elixir**,
One **stirs the River Vehicle**,
**Stirs the gentle winds**,
Applies the **Earth’s fire**,
And refines the **true essence of the Li Palace**.

When **true qi** merges with **true essence**,
It is the **prenatal yang qi** subduing the **postnatal yin essence**,
And the **yin essence** also merges with **true qi**,
Transforming into the **holy fetus**.

For **true qi** is born from **true essence**,
As **child-qi**—
When **qi** returns to **essence**,
It is likened to **child entering the mother’s womb**.

It is said: *"The child clings to the mother and comes,
The mother clings to the child and remains—
Child and mother embrace,
Spirit and qi depend on each other."*

It is the **internal true fire**,
The **external application of yin-symbol yang-fire**—
When **internal and external** refining occurs,
The **holy fetus** is formed—
As in the saying: *"When lead is nearly exhausted, mercury also dries,
Transformed into one piece of purple gold frost."*

The **great Dao of gold elixir** differs from the **Dao of birth**—
Only in this inversion of **nature’s transformations**,
And overturning of **Heaven and Earth**.

All those with **merit and virtue**,
With **opportunity and Dao**—
Upon encountering my **explanation**,
May all apply the **function**,
Without fear of **heterodox calamities**.

Yet the **Heavenly mechanism** is fully revealed here—
If there are those who **assist in virtue**,
And receive **Heaven’s illumination**,
Understanding this **meaning**—
They must not **lightly disclose** it,
Lest they incur **guilt and blame.»**

「Then the scripture speaks of *"the sovereign of ten thousand chariots"*—
This is the **original spirit** within the human body.

All people’s hearts desire
A single body’s peace and security,
A hundred years of vigor and strength—
Yet how can they know to **induce transformations**,
To **arouse emotions** and **generate life**,
While **lightly expending** their bodies in the world?

This **qi** is **hollow and floating**, thus **losing qi**;
This **spirit** is **agitated and restless**, thus **losing spirit**—
If the body’s survival is already scarce,
How much more so the **Dao of gold elixir**?

This **explanation** has already laid out
The **principles** of **foundation-building**, **self-refinement**, **forming the elixir**, **returning the elixir**, **jade nectar**, and the **small and great cosmic cycles**—
Detailed and clarified.
Those who follow the **Way of life**,
Who are **scholars and officials**,
Should cherish and never forget it—
Thus knowing its truth and practicing it to perfection.

Through this, **achievement and Dao** are attained,
And one becomes forever a **celestial immortal**,
Free from the **sufferings of the mortal world**—
Is this not most fortunate?
All should strive accordingly!

**Chapter Twenty-Seventh: Constantly Do Good to Save Others**
**Good deeds** leave no **traces** to be followed,
**Good words** bear no **flaws** to be censured,
**Good instruction** requires no **plans or strategies**,
**Good concealment** has no **locks or keys** yet cannot be opened,
**Good binding** has no **ropes or knots** yet cannot be undone.

Thus the **sage** constantly does good to save others,
And so **never abandons anyone**;
Constantly does good to save all things,
And so **never discards anything**.

This is called **"inheriting clarity."**

Therefore, the **good person** is the **teacher** of the **not-good**,
And the **not-good** is the **resource** of the **good**.
If one does not **honor their teacher**,
And does not **cherish their resource**,
Even great wisdom may lead to **great confusion**.

This is called **"the essential subtlety."**

The **sage’s heart** seeks only within themselves,
Not in others.

In their **application to affairs and things**,
They act without **non-action**—
Whatever arises, they respond accordingly,
With no **deficiency within**,
And no **harm done to others without**.

As the *Yijing* says:
*"When the time is to stop, one stops;
When the time is to act, one acts—
In **motion and stillness**, one does not lose the **proper timing**,
Their **Dao** is **radiant and clear**."*
Is this not such a person?

In their **conduct**, when the time is right to act,
They simply act—
No **trace** of their origin before,
No **path** of their destination behind—
How could **traces** possibly remain?

Their **conduct’s goodness** is such.

In their **words**, when the time is right to speak,
They simply speak—
No **humiliation** seen within themselves,
No **shame** left for others—
How could **flaws** possibly persist?

Their **words’ goodness** is such.

As for **matters requiring calculation**,
And **affairs needing strategy**—
Measured by **reason**,
Judged by **sentiment**,
Following **reason** to apply,
Conforming to **sentiment** to halt—
When much is fitting, much is done;
When little is fitting, little is done—
Why bother with **planning and scheming**?
This **responsive action without deliberation**,
Where **self and others dissolve**—
Is this not the **good calculation**?

Further, there are **matters requiring closure and binding**—
For others, if not **closed**, there is **chaos**;
If not **bound**, there is **dispersion**—
Yet the **sage** cuts off all **external connections**,
And **no internal thoughts** arise—
**Perfect and complete**, is this not the **good concealment**?

Though there are no **ropes or knots** to constrain,
No **locks or keys** to guard—
Yet there is no **gap** for others to exploit,
As if **sealed tightly and unassailable**,
Their **impenetrability** is such.
Is this not the **sincere unity of Heavenly principle**,
With **no vulnerabilities** to be seized?

This **number** of ways—
They follow **natural Heaven**, untainted by human **artifice**,
And so their effects are such.

Essentially, **internal cultivation** and **external emulation**,
**Self-correction** without **other demands**—
This is how one **establishes themselves and others**,
With **no one left behind**;
This is how one **perfects themselves and things**,
With **no talent wasted**.

Their **benevolence in saving and benefiting others**—
How could it be otherwise?

This is all from **self-illuminating virtue**,
And **extending it** to **govern people and things**—
Is this not **reiterating their clarity**?

Yet the **good person** initially does not **know themselves**—
The **good person** **forgets** **self and others**,
Thus the **not-good** are **moved** and **revere them as teacher**.
The **good person** is also not **self-satisfied**—
Seeing the **not-good**, the **good person** takes them as **resource**,
Following what is **good** and correcting what is **not**—
Thus the **good person** **advances in goodness**,
Until they reach the **domain of supreme transformation and divine change**.

If **common folk** **rely on their own abilities**,
**Boast of their own skills**—
Seeing the **good**, they **ignore** them as if nothing,
Not knowing to **revere them as models**;
Seeing the **not-good**, they **discard** them as if they were trash,
Even **despising** them and deeming them unworthy—
Not knowing *"to see the virtuous and strive to equal them,
To see the unvirtuous and reflect inward"*—
Though **good and evil** differ,
Their **teachers and resources** for **self** remain the same.

Such as this—
Not **honoring their teacher**,
Not **cherishing their resource**—
Are they not the **foolish and self-indulgent**,
The **lowly and self-absorbed**?
Are they not truly the **bewildered**?

**Goodness** is **learned from teachers**,
**Evil** is **warned against**—
Whatever arises is **beneficial to oneself**,
No person lacks **benefit to the body**.

This is truly the **essential method of self-cultivation**,
The **wonderful Dao of bodily governance**—
All should **strive** accordingly!

This **understanding of the sage’s words** is **universally applicable**.
The **principles of affairs and things**,
Are the **Dao of life and death**—
**Substance and function** are inherently **unified**,
**Root and branch** originally **inseparable**.

As said, **good conduct** leaves no **traces**—
Extended to the **flow of spiritual qi**,
The **River Vehicle** moving **on its own**—
This is also so.

If there are **traces or signs**,
It belongs to **forced manipulation and deliberate meditation**—
Not the **free movement of the River Vehicle**,
Nor the **natural alignment with Heaven’s Dao**.

It says *"good words bear no flaws"*—
Meaning **no laws can be spoken**, this is called **Dharma transmission**,
Or *"the intent of the Ancestral Teachers from the West."*

Confucius said:
*"How does Heaven speak?
The **four seasons** move in their course,
The **ten thousand things** come to life."*

If there are **flaws to be censured**,
It means there are **words visible**—
Not the **sage’s silent comprehension and spiritual resonance**.

The **Buddhist School** says:
*"The **Dao** is originally **without words**,
Yet people have **spoken it into ruin**."*
This is its meaning.

It says *"good calculation requires no scheming"*—
The **numbers of the cosmic cycle**,
Are merely **symbolic names** for **three hundred transformations**,
In truth, there are no **hexagrams or strategies** to calculate;
If there are, they are not **natural fire and timing**.

It says *"good concealment has no locks"*—
This is the **original chaos** unbroken,
The **original spirit** **silent and motionless**,
The **original qi** **obscure and still**,
Returning to the **beginning of the Primordial Origin**,
To **bind the fetus** and thus become **sage**.

「If there is **closing**, there must be **opening**—
This is not the **Dao** of **internal cultivation**.

It says *"good binding requires no cord or constraint"*—
The **spirit** clings to the **qi** and congeals,
The **life** depends on the **nature** and abides.
When **spirit and qi** embrace,
They return to the **Primordial Pole (Tai Ji)**,
Binding into a **rice-grain-sized pearl**—
The **body of the Yang Spirit**.

If there is **artificial binding**, it is forced together,
Not the **natural coalescence** of the **qi**,
And thus cannot **restore life and return to the true self**—
Yet its **effects** are as described.

The **essence of cultivation and nourishment** lies simply in:
*"Seeing the good, one shifts toward it;
Encountering faults, one corrects them."*
Taking **patterns from the good and the bad**,
And **reflecting inwardly** as the **method**.

If one **boasts of talent** and **relies on wisdom**,
**Disdains the Dao** and **tramples others**,
Holds no **reverence for the teacher**,
Nor **cherishes the resources**,
Even with **talent and wisdom**,
One remains a **foolish and ignorant man**,
And will **never attain the Dao**.

Here lies the **subtle essence of cultivation**—
The **sage and the common man** share the **same path**.

**Chapter Twenty-Eighth: Constant Virtue Never Departs**

*"Know its **masculine** aspect, hold to its **feminine** aspect,
To become the **valley of the world**;
To become the **valley of the world**,
**Constant virtue** never departs,
And returns to the **infant state**.

*Know its **white**, hold to its **black**,
To become the **model of the world**;
To become the **model of the world**,
**Constant virtue** remains unerring,
And returns to the **Primordial Non-Polarity (Wu Ji)**.

*Know its **prosperity**, hold to its **humiliation**,
To become the **abyss of the world**;
To become the **abyss of the world**,
**Constant virtue** is then complete,
And returns to **primordial simplicity (Pu)**."*

**Pu** disperses to form **vessels**;
The **sage** employs them as **officials and leaders**.
Thus, the **great method** is never severed.

In the **Dao of cultivation and refinement**,
**Qi** originates from the **Yang**.
Operating the **River Wheel (He Che)**, proceeding by **Child-Midnight (Zi-Wu)**.
When the **lead-qi** is fully extracted,
And the **mercury-essence** is sufficient,
This is when **lead and mercury merge into one qi**—
Now, **merging the masculine** to **refine the elixir**,
But **suppressing the feminine** to **nourish the elixir** is even more crucial.

Hence it says: *"Know its **masculine**, hold to its **feminine**."*

The **masculine** is **Yang**;
The **feminine** is **Yin**.
When **Yin and Yang** harmonize,
And **masculine and feminine** resonate,
The **metal is hidden within the water**;
Then **water again generates metal**—
When the **metal-qi** is abundant,
The **tidal signals** arrive.
Its **momentum** is like a **valley and ravine**,
Flowing from above to below,
Just as the **valley and ravine** accumulate and overflow.

The **practitioner** knows that **Yang does not generate from Yang alone**,
But from **Yin**—
Thus, one does not **hold to the masculine** but **holds to the feminine**.

Over time, **subtle Yang gradually emerges**,
And the **Yin dross** is fully transformed,
Returning to the **constant virtue of restoring the root and life**,
Which **cannot be momentarily separated**.

From here, **Yin and Yang** intermingle,
Binding into the **immortal fetus**,
And thus **daily tempering and nourishing** to form the **infant**—
This is inevitable.
The *Wù Zhēn* says: *"Nurturing the feminine within the masculine to bind the sacred fetus"*—
This is it.

Once **lead and mercury** have merged,
And become **one unified essence**,
This **intermingling essence** is then **nourished in the Kūn Palace** (Kun Gong) for **refinement**,
And **true lead** is born.

This is called *"knowing its **white** and holding to its **black**"*.
The **white** is the **essence**;
The **black** is the **water**.

Before the **essence** is produced,
The **Kūn body** is inherently **void**—
When it **interacts with the Kān (Heavenly Water)**,
The **Kūn void** becomes **Kān (Abyssal Water)**.
Thus, **metal is born within the water**,
And relies on the **Kūn Mother** to **nourish and complete** it,
Hence it is called **mother-qi**.
The *Wù Zhēn* says: *"Extracting the white from the black as the elixir-mother"*—
This is it.

Once **true lead** is obtained,
One **activates a droplet of one’s own mercury** to greet it.
With **left hand lifting and right hand drawing**,
One **quietly awaits the White Tiger’s head** (Bai Hu Shou Jing).
If one **truly hears the thunderous rumblings from below**,
There is the **state of the elixir-heart piercing the day**,
And the **vast-qi towering above the heavens**—
I **still hold to my void and still abode**,
**Not the slightest agitation**,
This is the **time of refining essence into qi**.

Afterward, **operating the wheel**,
Ascending the **three vehicles (sānrú)**,
From the **double gates (shuāngguān)** of the **sacral spine**,
Up to the **mud pellet (nìwán)**,
Following the **four cardinal processes (Zi-Wu-Mao-You)**,
And **harmonizing the sequence of the four seasons**—
This is the **model of the world**.

All **birth, growth, contraction, and concealment** of **humans and things**,
Also **do not differ in the slightest** from the **heavenly transformations**.

From this, **ascending and descending**,
Sending it back to the **earthly cauldron** (tǔfǔ),
Transforming **manifest forms** into **non-manifest forms**,
And returning to the **Primordial Non-Polarity (Wu Ji)** of the **Heaven**.
This is the **moment of the Great Heavenly Cycle**—
The **jade-fluid elixir** is here.

At this time,
The **golden elixir** returns to the **mysterious orifice** (Xuànqiào),
And **merges with the true-one qi of the Azure Dragon** (Qīnglóng Zhēnyī),
Refining into the **non-dual Primordial Spirit**—
This is the **time of refining qi into spirit**.

In the **next layer of cultivation**—
The **Dao of refining spirit back to void**—
Only **mysterious and chaotic**,
**Nourishing the void and stillness**;
**Turbulent and profound**,
**Perfectly uniting principle and qi**;
**Transforming perception into wisdom**,
**Merging sagehood with foolishness.**»

「A single day and night,
Speak not lightly, think not otherwise—
Like a dullard husband, utterly without perception.
Even if insults come again and again,
Stand as if unaware, as if ignorant—
Just as Shun dwelt in the deep mountains,
No different from a wild man of the hills.
This is the **honor of the perfected human**,
The **humiliation of the perfected sage**.

Without this, one cannot **nourish the void** and **align with the Dao**.
Thus it is said:
*"Speak, and the spirit-qi scatters;
The mind in turmoil, the fire of cultivation grows cold.
He who knows the **Law of Return**—
His golden treasure weighs like mountains."*

If one speaks recklessly, if one harbors a single thought,
It is like fleeing the elixir.
The **Dao grows higher, the path grows more perilous**.
At this stage of elixir refinement, it is the most dangerous ground—
Hence, ancient sages, after attaining fruition,
Feigned deafness and madness, acted as fools and lunatics—
All for the sake of **nourishing the void** and **aligning with the Dao**.
Why else would they endure such suffering?

Thus, the mind must hold nothing—
This is the **valley of the world**.
As the **valley of the world**, it must be colder than ice,
Clearer than water,
And only then will the **eternal mysterious virtue** be fully realized.

Yet **true emptiness is not emptiness, subtle being is not being**.
First, from **non-being to being**,
Then from **being back to non-being**,
Finally, where **being and non-being stand not at all**.
This is the **Dao of returning to the Primordial Simplicity** from the **Great Polarization (Tai Ji)**,
The **Way of restoring the origin and returning to the root**.

Though it **converges into one**, it **disperses into ten thousand**.
Thus, **endless generation**, **endless transformation**—
Where is not the **vessel** present?
Where is not the **Primordial Simplicity** dispersed?
This is the **saying of the Primordial Simplicity dispersing into vessels**.

The sage employs this—
Not valuing the vessel but dispersing the Primordial Simplicity—
For **emptiness and stillness** are the **master of the body**,
The **total holder of all transformations**,
Like the sole authority in the world of men.
It is also said, *"The great measure does not cut"*—
For the **Dao in its wholeness** encompasses all without omission,
Fulfills all without excess—
Sufficient for governance.
If one were to **cut into it**, it would be artificial contrivance,
Not the original **nature of Heaven**.
The sage does not cut—
Only returns to the **Primordial Chaos of Heaven**.

Do the students understand?
When viewed alongside the **chapter on Confucius’ virtue**, one sees
The essence of **refining essence, refining qi, refining spirit** is all here.

Still, its subtleties must be further explained:
*"In days past, the master’s oral instruction:
Only **concentrate the spirit** and enter the **qi-cavity**."*

If one does not **return the light and illuminate the elixir field (Dan Tian)**,
The **golden water** will surely become turbid.
Once one knows to **concentrate the spirit in the Kūn Palace (the lower elixir field)**,
Yet sometimes **halts and does not persist**,
The **water and fire** will scatter—
Where then will the **true-one qi of the Primordial Heaven** arise?

Though **concentrating the spirit** is essential,
**Regulating the breath** must not be neglected.
If one knows to **concentrate the spirit in the qi-cavity**
But does not know to **adjust the inhalation and exhalation**,
Descending into the **Yin-latch orifice (Yin Kēi)**,
Though the spirit may dwell, the breath will not flow freely—
Without **fanning the wind and stirring the fire**,
The **common breath** will stagnate while the **true breath** emerges,
The **common mind** will die while the **true mind** is born.

Moreover, the **true fire** depends entirely on the **true breath**—
Without the **true breath** to fan it,
Not only will the **water and fire** remain unclean,
But the **golden embryo** will fail to refine.

Once the **spirit is concentrated** and the **breath is regulated**,
One knows where to **return**—
At the moment when the **spirit is harmonized** and the **qi is unobstructed**,
As if **Heaven has not yet opened**,
Dark and indistinct—
Only then can all **wandering thoughts and turbid qi** be gathered and purified,
Like the **eclipse of the sun and moon**, revealing a new vitality.
Thus, **thread by thread, weave by weave**,
At the moment of **no awareness**,
Suddenly there is **awareness**—
This is the **foundation of the Great Polarization (Tai Ji)**,
The **manifestation of the Mysterious Pass (Xuàn Guān)**,
The **first stir of the Primordial Yang**.
At this moment, if one can **grasp it firmly, hold it steadily**,
This is the **technique of seizing mist and catching clouds**.

The **Dan Jing** says, *"When the time arrives, the spirit knows,"*
And again, *"The true child is alive"*—
This is precisely what is meant.

At this moment, one must **seize it immediately**—
If even a moment is delayed,
The **post-heaven awareness** will arise again,
And it will no longer be fit for the **golden elixir**.

This **critical juncture** must be grasped
When all **affiliations are abandoned** and **not a single thought arises**—
Only then can the **true intention** find it,
And the **true pure medicine** be obtained.

It must be **stillness upon stillness,沉沉沉沉 (sinking deeper and deeper)**—
At the moment of **no awareness, no perception**,
One seeks **awareness and perception**—
Only then may it be attained.

If it is said, *"Not a single thought arises,"*
Then why seek with the **intention**?
Is it not that **intentionally seeking** falls into **post-heaven awareness and spirit**?

Yet the **true intention** is like **hidden fire**—
Though unseen, the fire is present.
It is merely **triggered by the mechanism**, and the spirit follows naturally—
Such is the **spontaneous response**.

If one says the **true intention is indeed intentional**,
It falls into **rigidity**.
If one says the **true intention is truly without intention**,
It falls into **empty vacuity**.

Between **intention and no intention**, the student must **understand it naturally**.

The *Yijing* says:
*"Motionless and still,
Yet responsive and penetrating."*
Only then is it **true knowing, true awareness**—
All done by the **true intention**.

Though the **true intention** arises from the **true heart**,
The heart must be **empty, luminous, and responsive**—
Neither increased by **having** nor decreased by **lacking**.
With this **true heart**, there is **true intention**.
With this **true intention**, there is **true breath**.

One must possess **enlightened illumination**,
Never missing the **opportune moment**—
Then each refinement will bring its own **growth and benefit**.

At this stage, if one **constantly seizes the moment**,
The **true yang** will naturally arise—
Still, one must **refine oneself and await the time**,
Not daring to harbor even a **trace of seeking movement**,
Lest the **post-heaven awareness and spirit** intrude—
Then the **Primordial Heaven’s utmost yang essence**,
The **true-one qi**,
Will, through **long-term cultivation and accumulation**,
Naturally produce the **great medicine**—
Capable of **returning youth and reversing aging.**»

「One must fear only **not** being willing to **accumulate merit and practice diligence**—
To **establish external cultivation** would be vain.
**Uphold propriety and rectify customs**—
To **cultivate inner virtue** is the only foundation for reception.

The common saying goes:
*"One fears not the single act, but the accumulation;
One fears not the sudden, but the forced combination."*
Truly, these words are profound.

Students who wish to grasp the **Dao/Way’s purpose** must not merely listen to the claim that **"nature alone suffices."**

**Chapter Twenty-Ninth: Removing Excess and Extremity**
*"If one seeks to take the world and act to do so,
I see it as a matter of necessity, not choice.*
*The world is a **divine instrument**—
It cannot be **willed** nor **grasped**.
To **will** it is to **undermine** it;
To **grasp** it is to **lose** it.
Thus, things either **act** or **follow**, **draw in** or **expel**, **strengthen** or **weaken**.
Therefore, the **Sage** removes the **excessive**, the **luxurious**, the **extreme**—
The **Dao/Way** is inherently **soundless and odorless**, pure and serene by nature.
Those who cultivate the **Dao/Way** must also **not know and not perceive**,
Purely yielding to **nature**—
This is the **mind-seal** of all ancestors, from the **Primordial Beginning** to this day,
Unalterable and beyond deviation.

Yet, how unlike the **heterodox sects and false schools** of the world!
They mock our **Dao/Way**, calling it **solitary cultivation of emptiness and refinement**,
Ultimately leading to **barren voidness and uselessness**—
How could I not ponder this?
*"If one seeks to take the world and enforce **artificial governance**,
I see it as a matter of necessity, not choice—
The more one enforces, the more one is driven to necessity."*
Indeed, though the world be vast,
Its **divine framework** is what precedes it.
The **Primordial Dao/Way** is the **silent natural**—
The world is the **divine instrument’s** boundary;
The **divine instrument** is the **world’s sovereign**—
The world may be **willed**, but the **divine instrument** may not.

If one **wills** it,
At first, there will be **chaos and many affairs**,
And in the end, **moral collapse and transgression**,
While **Heaven’s virtue** is utterly abandoned—
This is precisely how **willing** leads to **undermining**.

Consider: **Artificial governance** brings ruin,
But **non-action** achieves success—
**Grasping** disrupts the **constant**,
Yet **non-grasping** attains the **Dao/Way**—
How much more so, since the **Dao/Way** originates from **Heaven**,
And **Heaven’s Dao/Way** is **non-action**,
While **spontaneous transformation** arises within it—
How could it be otherwise?

Observe the time of birth:
The **Primordial Yang** (*乾元*) initiates creation—
Sometimes **yang** departs and **action** precedes;
Sometimes **yin** arrives and **following** comes after.
**Motion** and **stillness** mutually root each other,
With **inevitability** in their nature.

As for **qi**—
When it **expands**, it naturally **contracts**;
When it **draws in**, it naturally **expels**—
**吸** then **呴** arises effortlessly;
**呼** then **吹** unfolds serenely.
Thus, **vital breath** flows freely,
And **life-force** endures eternally.

Yet, **endowments and receptions** differ—
**Strength** and **softness** are not the same—
Some receive **abundant qi** and possess **vigorous essence**,
Others receive **sparse qi** and have **weakened essence**—
All these are **post-heaven disparities**.

Since things are born with their own distinctions,
Sometimes they **ascend**, their **qi-machinery** flourishing upward,
Sometimes they **descend**, their **qi-machinery** naturally collapsing downward—
All these are the **natural workings of Heaven’s Dao/Way**,
Not something **human effort** can force.

Though at the **initial stage** there may be traces of **coercion**,
Yet one must follow its **momentum** and **timing**—
**Act** when it can be done,
**Cease** when it must be stopped—
**Coercion** within **yielding to nature**,
Which remains **unfailing** over the long term.

This is also what the **Sage** knows when **harvesting medicine and refining elixir**—
In all things, **remove the already excessive**,
**Remove the too luxurious**,
**Remove the too extreme**—
Always returning to **moderation**,
Always maintaining **harmony**.

Though it may be said **"artificial governance" exists**,
It is also the same as **"non-action"**;
Though it may be said **"action occurs"**, it is also the same as **"non-action"**.

Thus, **having and not-having mutually generate**,
Only then can one speak of the **Great Dao/Way**.

This is the **Great Dao/Way of non-action**—
**Non-action** refers to the **study of nurturing the Primordial** (*先天养性*);
Yet it is also **action**—
**Action** refers to the **craft of refining the post-heaven** (*后天炼命*).

One must know that **action and non-action**,
Though their **cultivation methods** differ,
The **sovereign principle** within them must never be **disturbed**—
If **disturbed**, it is **not moderation**.
Whether **action** or **non-action**,
Both are **not** the **Dao/Way**.

Only when the **sovereign principle** remains **unshaken and undisturbed**,
Knowing **timing and discerning momentum**,
Advancing when **opportunity** presents,
Retreating when **difficulty** arises—
Then **non-action** is achieved,
And **action** is also attained.

What is the **sovereign principle**?
It is the **divine instrument of the world**.

If humans can **grasp its origin**,
And **return** to the **undifferentiated and unfathomable**,
**Empty and luminous** without **obscurity**—
At first, **action** is **action**,
And at the end, **non-action** is **non-action**.

Otherwise, if one **universally claims** that **"non-action is natural"**, then why did **Confucius** bother to speak of **Dao/Way**?
Why did he speak of **necessity’s diligent practice**?
Why did he speak of **choosing virtue and firmly holding it**?

Knowing the **method of self-cultivation**,
Its **foundation** lies in **nurturing life and essence**—
The **cultivation of life and essence** requires **rest and effort**,
Not **forcibly distinguishing** between them—
All depends on **human discernment** of its **virtue/power**.

As in **governing the state**:
**Peace** is maintained through **ritual and music**,
**Chaos** is suppressed through **arms and warfare**—
**Responding to seasons** and **acting in accordance with Heaven**,
Then **success** will surely come—
**Left and right** will **flow like a source**,
And in all things, **fitness** will be found.

This is the **Dao/Way** that can be spoken to the **wise**,
But is **difficult** for the **rigid and dull-witted** to grasp.

**Chapter Thirtieth: The Fruit of Virtue**
*"Aiding a ruler with the **Dao/Way**,
One does not **coerce the world with arms**—
Such **endeavors** tend to **return in kind**:
Where the **teacher** abides, **briers and thorns** grow—
After great **military campaigns**, **harsh years** must follow.
Thus, the **fruit of virtue** is **simplicity** alone—
One **dares not** use it for **coercion**.
**Simple** yet **not arrogant**,
**Simple** yet **not boastful**,
**Simple** yet **not forced**,
**Simple** yet **not coercive**—
When things **flourish**, they **age**—
This is called **not the Dao/Way**,
And **not the Dao/Way** will **soon perish**.

In the **highest antiquity**,
Each ruled their own **state**,
Each **remembered their people**—
**Harmonious and bright** (*熙熙皞皞*),
They **shared** in **Heaven’s peaceful order** without **affairs**;
**Self and others** were **forgotten in unity**,
**Boundaries dissolved**—
How could there be **warfare** then?

When **shared labor** led to **disorder** and **conquests** began,
**Chiyou** (*蚩尤*) **transgressed** and **arms** were **raised**.
Then, **civilized governance** had **jade and silk**,
**Martial governance** had **weapons and armor**—
**Order** was maintained through **ritual and music**,
**Chaos** was suppressed through **dry weapons and blades**—
Thus, **courts** must **balance civil and martial** **virtue/power** together.»

The **virtuous** sovereign of the **Dao/Way**, enlightened and in high station,
Assisted the flourishing court, aiding in **harmonious governance**,
Serving the sovereign with **Dao/Way** alone, never enforcing strength upon the world.

Why is this so?
For he who slays another’s father and brother,
Another will slay his father and brother in return.
Human hearts yearn to return to **harmony**,
**Heaven’s order** favors restoration.
Grievances and vengeance know no end.

Moreover, where armies pass,
The people suffer harm;
Where troops march,
Even chickens and dogs are left desolate.
Thus, slaughter and death multiply—
Corpses fill great rivers, blood stains long walls,
From noble to common, all become dry bones.
The number of those who die exceeds those who live.
Wells grow desolate, fields lie fallow, and brambles take root.

Furthermore, the **killing qi** severely injures **Great Harmony** (*太和*),
The **perverse and rebellious winds** provoke **Heaven’s wrath**.
Thus, **yin-yang** fails to harmonize,
Rain and sun lose their proper time—
Droughts and floods come in succession, calamities follow,
Famine and hardship press upon the people,
Life is not worth a morning or an evening.
The ancients said: *"After a great army, there will surely be a year of famine,"*
A fate that must come to pass.

Yet when hunger and cold press hard,
Banditry grows daily;
When years are barren and calamitous,
Rebellious crowds rise—
Sometimes, war cannot be avoided.
The ancients said: *"Warfare values swiftness, not hesitation,"*
Thus, those skilled in war act decisively.
A **ren-yi** army arrives like timely rain,
Relieving those in dire straits with welcome offerings.
As when **King Wu** in a single campaign pacified the realm,
His purpose was merely to uphold **Dao/Way** and destroy the tyrant’s leader—
How dare he indulge in slaughter for a moment’s gain,
Or seize strength for personal glory!
If victory comes, do not boast—
Boasting breeds a love of war;
Do not self-praise—
Self-praise harbors martial arrogance.
Even if he subdues tyrants with ease,
Elevates the people to prosperity,
This is but the duty of a general to stabilize the state,
