Thus the sage is square yet does not cut,
sharp yet does not pierce,
straight yet does not overreach,
bright yet does not dazzle.

Heaven and Earth act without intent yet transform and nourish;
the sovereign rules without action yet achieves harmony.
This is the Dao of *wuwei*—
the great principle and law by which the sage opened Heaven and Earth,
harmonized the world, and ordered all things.

The ruler governs the myriad people,
regulating all beneath Heaven—
nothing surpasses this.
If one resorts to *youwei* [action],
governance is not true governance,
rule is not true rule.
Though literature may flourish and achievements gleam,
one cannot achieve the *xīxī yùyù* [harmonious and radiant] age of shared joy and prosperity.

Thus the *Tàishàng* [Supreme Sage] said:
*“Governance is rectification”—*
rectifying others through one’s own rectitude.

From ancient times, those who ruled the people
established human norms and ordered Heaven’s patterns,
acting as if knowing yet not knowing,
acting as if acting yet not acting—
letting Heaven’s natural impulses move freely.
They never forced clever schemes,
invented measures, or promulgated laws.
Yet through a single virtue, they resonated in harmony,
transmitting meaning beyond words.

Thus its governance is dim and unassuming,
as though simple and unknowing.
Yet the people’s trust and sincerity
remain pure and unchanging,
retaining the ancient virtue of old.
The ruler governs through non-action,
the people transform through non-action—
ruler and ruled alike rest in the tranquil Heaven,
oh, how splendid this peace!

If the ruler instead strives with vigor,
exhausting effort to govern,
rooting out wickedness while elevating the worthy,
recording even minor virtues and punishing grave offenses,
with rewards and punishments as clear as ice and mirror,
and oversight as stern as divine judgment—
then governance becomes meticulous,
no one escapes its scrutiny—
yet is this not also worthy of weight?

But when the ruler demands excessive precision,
the people respond with cunning schemes,
boasting their petty cleverness.
The ruler acts, the people imitate—
how difficult it is to govern the people’s hearts!

If the source is not purified above,
the root cannot be rectified below.
Non-action is the pristine truth of the primal Heaven,
action is the contrived artifice of later cultivation.
The effects of dimness and meticulousness are thus pure and mixed.

This is clear: one principle alone—
to split it is error.

Before Heaven’s *Tàijí* divided,
before purity was split,
there was no name for yin and yang,
no distinction of good and evil.
The *Yì* says:
*“Simple, thus easily known;
frugal, thus easily followed.”*
This is why such governance can endure.

But when the primal *Tàipú* is incomplete,
when yin and yang span beginning to end,
when misfortune and fortune alternate—
misfortune within fortune, fortune within misfortune—
this is how calamity and blessing cycle endlessly.

Thus action is not necessarily unvirtuous,
but when things reach their limit, they reverse.
The interplay of yin and yang is inherent.
Who can know the ultimate end and preserve true governance?

Moreover, when rectitude returns, it becomes eccentric;
when virtue reverses, it becomes ominous.
Non-action’s governance is pure as Heaven.
Action’s governance is mixed with human contrivance.
Mixed with human contrivance—
rectitude contains eccentricity, virtue contains ominousness.
Its mechanisms arise from subtle beginnings,
its responses unfold through influence,
its momentum is relentless.

No wonder deceit and guile become habitual,
ingrained until none awaken.
This has been so for ages.

Thus the Sage governs the world,
rooting governance in the Way of non-action,
rectifying himself to transform others.
The square is square without knowing its squareness—
perhaps it masters adaptability without rigid rules?
The austere is austere without knowing its austerity—
perhaps it blends with the common, its light unbroken?
At times, uprightness is not blind compliance,
nor is it unchecked indulgence.
Upholding principle in action, never daring excess—
its rigid yet revered norms are truly awe-inspiring.

As for transforming all beings,
its benevolence extends to the four quarters,
like stars and clouds in radiant display,
yet it hides itself, never flaunting its brilliance.
How does it vanish its traces and silence its voice?

This is non-action as essence,
naturalness as function—
governing through desire, applying principle.
When the winds of the four directions stir,
who could fail to join in harmonious transformation,
to wander together in the ancient Heaven?

Is this not so?

The Dao is called the Great Dao,
the elixir is called the Golden Elixir—
both are nameless, formless.

In Heaven, it is the clear and empty *qi*;
in man, it is the void and natural.
From beginning to end of cultivation,
nothing transcends this.

If one knows the boundless and indistinct
is the root of the Great Dao,
the origin of the Golden Elixir—
and from the utmost stillness and sincerity,
nurtures the undifferentiated, the unknowing,
the thoughtless and desireless true essence—
then one’s nature, emotions, vital essence, and spirit
are all things of the primal *Tàihé* *qi*.
With this to cultivate the Dao, the Dao is complete;
with this to refine the elixir, the elixir is perfected—
what strange danger or peril remains?

But if one ignores non-action as foundation,
fixating only on action as achievement,
then knowledge never ceases,
disturbance only multiplies—
how could one avoid falling into the later, shaped, and chaotic?

The Supreme Sage likens governance to the Dao,
compares the people to the body.
Cultivating the Dao through primal non-action
forges an unbreakable golden body;
cultivating the Dao through later awareness
how could it avoid duality of spirit?
Even if refined well,
it is but a preserved corpse—
how could it transcend yin and yang,
escape birth and death,
and become an immortal for all ages?

Worse still, if one falls into action,
the *Tàijí* divides and yin and yang arise,
yin and yang separate and good and evil emerge—
then calamity and blessing alternate.

Who knows that the ultimate attainment of cultivation,
though it may require some action,
must arise from action within non-action,
from function within non-function,
only then avoiding extremes?

Mencius said: *“Act, yet do not force.”*
This is the essence of cultivation.

The human heart—
when one aspect moves, another stirs;
when one aspect is yin, another is yang.
Evil and rectitude, good and bad—
they cycle and interweave without end.
Thus rectitude contains eccentricity,
virtue contains ominousness.
Only in undivided oblivion,
where no distinction of rectitude and eccentricity exists,
can good and evil vanish.
Otherwise, rectitude returns as eccentricity,
virtue reverses as ominousness.

Zhuangzi said:
*“Heaven honors non-action as supreme,
man burdens himself with action.”*
Thus, when action arises,
it must return to non-action
to avoid the disaster of overturning the elixir.

Alas, the common folk—
speak of the elixir, and they cling to the *dāntián*;
fixate on the River Vehicle’s path,
confined within the body—
their failure to awaken to non-action’s essence
has endured for ages.

Only the sage understands the Dao of cultivation.
Though there are fire and timing, medicines and elixirs,
dragon-tiger pairings, male-female unions,
cauldrons, furnaces, zithers, and swords—
all these names and forms are but the traps and snares for fish and rabbits:
use them to catch the fish and rabbits,
but once the fish and rabbits are in hand,
forget the traps and snares.
If one clings to names and forms,
they are not the Dao.

Thus, square when square,
honest when honest,
straight when straight,
bright when bright—
yet all must return to non-action,
to doing nothing while doing,
to merging into the boundless void.

Let the student take the Dao of natural non-action as essence.
Only when essence is established may action follow.
Even with action, it remains non-action.

Do you know?
Do you believe?

**Chapter 59: Eternal Life and Longevity**
To govern humanity and serve Heaven, nothing surpasses frugality.
Only frugality is early cultivation.
Early cultivation is called accumulating virtue.
Accumulating virtue ensures nothing is unconquered.
Nothing unconquered means its limits are unknown;
unknown limits mean one can possess a realm.
Possessing a realm’s foundation means eternal life and longevity.

The way to govern humanity is the way to serve Heaven—
Heaven and humanity are fundamentally one *qi*.
Thus, governing humanity is the means to serve Heaven,
and serving Heaven does not go beyond governing humanity.
Do not say Heaven’s Dao is distant—
it dwells within humanity’s nearest path.
If you do not know Heaven’s Dao,
first observe human nature.
To exhaust human affairs is to fulfill Heaven’s Dao.
Though high and low may seem distant,
if the people are settled, Heaven’s will is unified.

Its essence lies in prioritizing agriculture and roots,
teaching the people to till and sow first.
For the people are the foundation of the state,
and food is the people’s Heaven.
When frugality is practiced,
clothing and food are abundant,
and families are secure.
As Mencius said:
*“Cultivate the five grains,
and when the grains ripen, the people thrive.”*
Again he said:
*“When the sage governs the world,
making grain and fire as accessible as water,
how could the people fail to be benevolent?”*
Thus, those in power must urgently practice frugality,
so the people may take joy in their work,
live in peace,
and nurture life while honoring death.

Before they even see or hear,
their hearts are already served,
and they willingly turn toward it,
as if feasting on the finest sacrifices.
This is virtue cultivated without speech,
elevated without proclamation.

Even with three years of labor and one of rest,
or nine years of labor and three of rest,
with abundant millet and sorghum,
brewing wine and *li* for offerings,
bestowing upon ancestors and conducting rites—
virtue accumulates layer upon layer.
Who else but this could achieve it?

Thus, the enlightened Heaven is reopened,
and boundless blessings are bestowed.
Naturally, the weak are protected,
the ignorant guided,
the chaotic subdued,
and the reckless preserved—
nothing they confront is unconquered.
Their advance is unstoppable,
no foe dares to resist.
Not only neighboring states bow in awe,
but distant lands also send envoys with offerings.
Eastward and westward, northward and southward,
their influence spreads without end—
who can fathom its limits?

Without limits, the Imperial Dao flourishes,
the realm is unshakable,
and the state is secured.
As the *Han Shu* says:
*“The Yellow River like a belt,
Tai Mountain like a whetstone.
The state endures in eternal peace,
love extending to descendants.”*
This is unerring truth.

When a person governs a state,
they have the means to obtain it—
and what is that means?
The *mother-qi* of the state.
Without mother-qi, how could one obtain the state?
This is the fundamental truth all should urgently discuss.
Before possessing a state, one must seek the mother;
having possessed it, one must cherish the mother.
A state’s mother is like a tree’s root,
water’s source—
enduring and unceasing.

This is the way of governing the world,
parallel to governing the self.
Those who cultivate the Dao
can embrace unity, still the breath, and harmonize the spirit,
first seeking the *mercury child* to find the *lead mother*,
then nurturing the *lead mother* with the *mercury child*,
until lead and mercury merge,
returning to the original,
reverting to the Primordial.
This is the way of deep roots and firm foundations—
eternal life and longevity.

Thus, the ordinary becomes sage,
and humanity becomes Heaven.

The way to govern the self is no different from governing the world.
This is exhausting human affairs to fulfill Heaven’s Dao—
*“Heaven and humanity are one *qi*,
mutually responsive and unified.
Yang descends from the void,
embracing me as master.”*
Its Dao is not beyond emptiness,
its function akin to tilling and sowing.

First, nourish, preserve, and inspect.
Then, use nature to govern emotions.
When water and fire blend,
kan and li unite,
pre-Heaven *qi* moves,
circulating the Microcosmic Orbit—
*“When Heaven and Earth’s union ceases,
a single point descends to the Yellow Court.”*

This draws the *kan*’s overflow into *li*’s void,
securing the foundation of life—
the work of human and immortal is complete.

This is like the frugal ruler clearing land and planting,
pruning and weeding before sowing the five grains.
Then, taking the *li*’s yin essence,
lowering it into the *kan*’s gate,
merging the *kan*’s yang *qi* with the *li*’s yin essence,
forming a family within the *dāntián* as medicine—
*“Where others lack, I possess;
where others are empty, I am full.”*

Until true lead emerges within,
using yang lead to subdue yin mercury—
its flighty nature no longer flees;
then using yin lead to nourish yang lead—
its sinking nature no longer sinks.
As the *Awakening to Reality* says:
*“The golden cauldron seeks to retain the cinnabar mercury,
the jade pool first descends the water-silver.”*

When lead and gold float and rise,
like dust in sunlight scattering,
the residual yang outside *kan* is exhausted,
returned to *li*’s palace.
Then the private mercury and recognition within *li*
are both dissolved,
restoring the pure yang elixir—
capable of ascending to the Han,
soaring through the heavens,
forming the divine embryo,
completing the immortal child.

「Although, its practice is not easily attained! At first, one must cultivate the will to nourish the *qi*—
like a farmer tilling the fields,
with no lack of toil and hardship.
Yet in the end, the spirit is tranquil and the *qi* is steady.

Within, the single principle is undivided and complete;
without, one adapts to the times and remains centered.
This is not done by chance once,
but aligns with the Great Dao/Way.

Through its refining nature and cultivating life,
one has long prepared to serve as a guest to the later-born—
thus severing all entanglements,
leaving not a thread behind,
fulfilling the human path to merge with the Heavenly *virtue/power*.

Like a state’s foundation,
one preserves sincere integrity and profound benevolence,
deep compassion and abundant *virtue/power*,
which enter the people’s hearts,
penetrating to the marrow and permeating the flesh—
the accumulation of such *virtue/power*,
its weight and depth,
know no bounds.

From this point onward,
nothing remains unremoved within oneself,
nothing unmastered by oneself—
Heaven’s embrace grows serene and settled,
walking the Five Phases with ease and composure.

Whether facing change or constancy,
one naturally follows one’s inherent station,
finding fulfillment in every place—
*"No matter where one goes, one finds oneself at ease."*

If this is so,
then using it to refine nature exhausts nature,
using it to cultivate life establishes life.

In the boundless void where no traces remain,
all phenomena stand complete and manifest—
truly, there is one whose depths are unknown.

The *Tàishàng* says:
*"Look inward to the heart—
the heart has no heart.
Look outward to the body—
the body has no body.
Look far to all things—
things have no things.
The emptiness of emptiness—
emptiness is not emptiness.
The nothingness of nothingness—
nothingness is not nothingness."*
Those who can awaken to this
may transmit the sacred Dao/Way.

This is the *"body transcends itself yet remains"*—
the body is like a state.
Just as a sovereign rules without action,
and thus stands upright before the people
to possess the state and the world,
so too with the *yin* essence within oneself,
long mingled with the father’s essence and mother’s blood—
without the *yang* *qi* of the Primordial Heaven,
it cannot generate or grow of its own accord.

Indeed, the *yin* essence of later birth
originally stems from the Primordial Heaven’s *yang*—
yet the *yin* essence is hard to stabilize,
and emotions/desires are easily unsettled.
Without the *qi* of Heaven and Earth’s external, refined *yang*,
one cannot forge it into the elixir,
nor achieve enduring life and deathlessness.

Thus it is said:
*"The mother of a lasting state,
can endure forever."*
Only the Sage,
with true *yin* and true *yang*,
merges the two *qi* into one,
refining a single grain of millet—
called the *golden elixir*,
*true lead*,
or the *White Tiger’s First Scripture*—
its essence is none other than the Primordial Heaven’s single *qi*.

Through ceaseless refining within the colored body—
endless melting and washing,
gradually extracting and condensing,
sometimes simmering, sometimes refining—
the *golden elixir* is formed,
its radiance clear and distinct—
those who *"steal the *qi* of Heaven and Earth to use as elixir mother"* are such.

This is the path of deep roots and firm foundations,
of enduring life and prolonged vision.

When the refined *yang* of Heaven and Earth
is merged with one’s true *qi*,
forming the sacred embryo,
the ancient immortals spoke of:
*"The Primordial Heaven’s single *yang* first moves,
stirring a single drop of one’s own mercury to greet it."*

Thus, inner contact and outer stimulation yield form,
outer contact and inner resonance yield spirit—
like a magnet drawing iron,
naturally aligning and joining.

The mercury child seeks the water palace
to find the lead mother;
once the mother is obtained,
it then relies on the child.

Child and mother in harmony,
clustered in the central palace,
the Great Elixir is formed,
and the Sage-Immortal is realized.

The beginning and end of elixir refining,
the Great Dao/Way has already fully revealed.
Scholars must carefully ponder and discern—
though the traces and symbols may seem alike,
their subtleties differ greatly.

Yet without the right time,
one cannot know;
without a true teacher’s guidance,
one cannot understand.

This requires the convergence of
Heaven’s *yuan* (缘),
Earth’s *yuan* (缘),
and human *yuan* (缘)—
only when the three *yuan* align
can one enter the chamber and begin the work.

Later scholars must first
accumulate sincerity and cultivate *virtue/power*,
empty themselves to seek a teacher—
thus may the three *yuan* converge and entry be made.
Do not rejoice at mere attainment
and lose the resolve to ascend.

Instead, take a vow of unwavering devotion,
press forward with single-minded effort—
progress may be slow,
but persistence is key.

At the very start,
there is no crack to enter,
no opening to seize—
it is like chewing on wax pills,
tasteless and insipid.

Zhūzǐ says:
*"To study, one must be resolute and tireless,
enduring hardship with patience."*

Long toil, and eventually,
the bitter turns sweet,
the stifled yields to joy—
the Dao advances, and the heart finds its gain.

At this juncture,
when *principle* and *desire* ride together,
and Heaven and man wage war,
it is most difficult to act.

Its advance and retreat,
lie at this critical pass.
If this pass is breached,
then the beauty of the ancestral temple,
the abundance of officials,
and the endless enjoyment of rewards—
as Confucius said—
shall be attained.

Never falter or grow weak,
for if one’s own spirit dwindles,
the gate of entry will forever remain closed.

Most importantly,
empty the heart,
enlarge the will,
stir the spirit,
and cultivate *virtue/power* and achievement,
refine nature and establish life.

Know that this is
the greatest of all matters between Heaven and Earth—
without immense strength,
it cannot be accomplished.

In days past, there was a couplet:
*"Brace iron shoulders to bear the Dao’s duty,
free stiff hands to craft the words."*

Ah!
Even in the world,
a single talent or skill—
the modest pursuit of scholarly fame—
requires toil and endurance,
using all one’s true spirit
to achieve great deeds,
before Heaven’s silent blessing can be earned—
how much more so for the Dao,
the greatest of all matters!

Thus the Buddha said:
*"I descended to this realm for the sake of the great *dharma* and great *yuan* (因缘),
and so do I now."*

Scholars, upon meeting a true teacher,
must with true heart and sincere intent
embody my words—
only then may they be counted
among the great men of this world.

**Chapter Sixty: Two Do Not Harm Each Other**
Ruling a great state is like cooking fresh delicacies.
Applying the Dao/Way to the world,
its *ghosts* are not numinous.
Not because its *ghosts* are not numinous,
but because its spirit does not harm others.
Not because its spirit does not harm others,
but because the Sage also does not harm others.

Thus, when two do not harm each other,
*virtue/power* naturally returns and merges.

The Dao/Way,
is the shared principle of all under Heaven.
Using this principle to cultivate oneself,
is the same as using it to govern the world.»

「I too am thus. If scholars, having met a true teacher,
must with true heart and sincere intent
embody my words—
only then may they be counted
among the great men of this world.

**Chapter Sixty: Two Do Not Harm Each Other**

To wish to establish oneself while establishing others,
to wish to attain while attaining for others—
without waiting for a shift in thought,
without delay in time,
how easy and simple it is!

Thus the *Tàishàng* (太上) says:
“Ruling a great state is like cooking fresh delicacies.”

When a state is vast,
its affairs must be complex,
its people numerous.
If one does not grasp the Dao/Way,
then it will inevitably become chaotic and convoluted—
like trying to unravel disordered silk,
the more one attempts to govern,
the more tangled it grows.

Only by applying the Dao/Way,
the shared principle of all under Heaven,
to cultivate one’s own person
and guide the multitude—
its logic flowing through all,
its *qi* permeating universally—
does one find the path most convenient.

Otherwise, if one merely relies on
laws and decrees,
prohibitions and schemes,
tactics and calculations,
and summons the world under such rules—
then in daylight, resentment festers among the people,
and their hearts grow deceitful and multifarious;
in darkness, the *ghosts* (鬼) are provoked,
and calamities—disasters and plagues—
pile up without end.

For the people are the masters of *ghosts* and *spirits* (神).
When rulers exact harsh levies,
indulge in tyranny,
and spread their venomous influence,
leaving the people without refuge—
then *ghosts* and *spirits*,
too, find no attachment,
and must rise in rebellion,
bringing ruin and sickness.
Thus did the *stone spirit* (石言) appear in *Jìn* (晉),
the *comet* (彗) in *Qí* (齐),
the *serpent battle* (蛇斗) in *Zhèng* (郑),
*Bó Yǒu* (伯有) become a scourge,
*Shēn Shēng* (申生) descend as a *ling* (灵) spirit,
the *Two Young Men* (二竖) fell into grave illness from dreams,
*Yǒu Shēn* (有莘) descended and *Guó* (虢) perished—
all these were acts of *ghosts* and *spirits*,
yet they arose because the ruler lacked the Dao/Way.

For those who govern the people,
if they truly cultivate the Dao/Way in themselves,
and transform the people with the Dao/Way—
though the *ghosts* (鬼) are *yīn* (阴) *qi*,
when they find their proper refuge,
even the most stubborn *ghosts* (鬼) will willingly follow.
The people will have no grievances,
and the *ghosts* will bring no calamities.
Mountains and rivers will not crumble,
and crops will not be plagued by monstrous anomalies.
In harmony and brightness,
one may sit and bask in the blessings of peace.

The *Shū* (书) says:
*“Our ancient sovereigns,
when they diligently cultivated their virtue/power,
there were no celestial calamities,
and the mountain rivers, ghosts and spirits,
all remained tranquil.”*

This is not because the *ghosts* are not numinous!
For *jīnglì wāngliáng* (魑魅魍魉),
as well as mountain spirits and water monsters,
all depend on some foundation,
and have their fixed offerings.
When left to their natural course,
they meddle in nothing.
Though they have spirit,
they have no means to act—
even if they act,
how could they ever prevail?

Thus, *yīn* and *yáng* (阴阳),
people and *ghosts*,
all frolic together
beneath the radiant Dao/Way of Heaven and Earth—
how could there be any harm to people?

Nor is it because the *spirits* do not harm others.
It is because the Sage,
with the Dao/Way in hand,
lacks the scheming wisdom of the petty,
nor the ostentatious benevolence of the self-aggrandizing.
They guard their own person with reverence,
cherish the natural bonds of humanity,
hold fast to respect,
act with simplicity,
avoiding all unnecessary entanglements—
not a single particle
ever harms another.

It lies in the harmony of *yīn* and *yáng*,
whereby people and things flourish,
and in the grandeur of rites and sacrifices,
whereby *ghosts* and *spirits* find peace.
In the realm of the unseen,
the two do not encroach upon each other.
Thus the world naturally submits
to the Sage’s virtue/power and returns to it.

Ah! The Dao/Way of *non-action* (無為),
both near and far—
taken from the self,
extended to all things—
is the way to rule the world,
and also the way to refine
the *Great Elixir of Return* (大還之丹).

In a world of great peace,
when governance reaches its highest principle,
and the realm is flourishing—
the ruler acts without action,
and the world transforms without coercion.
All *ghostly* mischief and *spiritual* malevolence
vanish without trace,
not because they are destroyed,
but because they are naturally dissolved
by the Dao/Way of *non-action*,
and their schemes collapse
without any means to act.
Droughts, floods, plagues, and epidemics
find no foothold.

In the human body,
the *ghost* is the *yīn* (阴) aspect—
still, silent, and unaware.
The *spirit* is the *yáng* (阳) aspect—
dynamic, active, and purposeful.

The great practitioner,
with a mind that encompasses all things yet remains without mind,
and emotions that respond to all yet are without emotion—
*yīn* within *yáng*,
*yáng* within *yīn*—
stillness without stillness,
movement without movement.
Movement and stillness
interact in their functions;
*yīn* and *yáng*
mutually sustain each other.

It is not that awareness is utterly absent
or that action is entirely non-existent.
Rather, within *non-awareness* (無覺),
there is true awareness;
within *non-action* (無為),
there is true action.

When it says *“its ghosts are not numinous”*,
it does not mean they are dull and lifeless.
For the awareness within *non-awareness*
is the true and equal awakening;
the action within *non-action*
is but the natural unfolding
of Heaven’s will.
How could it compare
to the false pretenses of those with awareness,
or the rigid adherence of those with action,
which only harm the original elixir?

When it says *“its spirit does not harm others”*,
it is not that the *spirit* does not harm others,
but that the Dao/Way of *non-action*
nurtures the innate purity of human life,
the ceaseless vitality of *yīn* and *yáng*,
the unending sincerity,
and the complete embodiment of all things.

Though there be creation and destruction,
in truth there is no loss or gain;
though there be fullness and emptiness,
in essence there is no increase or decrease.»

「This is what is meant by *unperturbed and unalarmed*—
free from worry and care.
How could it harm others?

It is not that the Sage does not harm others,
but rather that with the *vital impulse* of life’s essence,
they restore the original purity of existence;
that with the *harmonious trance* of 三昧 (*sāṃdhi/samādhi*),
they cultivate the *free-flowing elixir* of self-mastery.
Once the *Divine Fire* refines,
the spirits wail and demons shriek,
the malevolent forces retreat in terror—
the True Person emerges.
This is called *“mutual non-injury”*—
who could say it is unfit?

Both Heaven and Earth
reverence their virtue.
Ah! The interplay of *dark* and *bright* (*yīn* and *míng*),
not the *virtue/power* of spirits alone,
how could it reach such heights?

**Chapter Sixty-One: The Great Should Descend**
The great realm descends to the lesser—
the *pivot of the world*, the *receptive mother* of the world.
The *receptive mother* ever takes the *vigorous* (*yáng*) through stillness,
and stillness as its descent.
Thus, the great realm descends to the small realm,
and the small realm is taken by the great;
either descending to take,
or descending while taken.
The great realm seeks only to *enfold* others,
the small realm seeks only to *submit* to others.
When both attain their desires,
the great is rightly suited to descend.

The *Tàishàng* speaks of *cultivating the Dao/Way and refining the elixir*—
all must be guided by *gentleness*,
and anchored in *stillness*.
Though it may be said that *gentleness* is useless weakness,
and *seclusion* hard to achieve,
yet at the outset of *meditative sitting*,
movement must arise from stillness,
and *rigidity* from *gentleness*—
only then is the true Dao/Way revealed.

The analogy *“the great realm descends”* speaks of water,
which has both ascent and descent—
the water above must flow downward
before it finds its end.
If the great realm humbles itself,
without a trace of arrogance or pretense,
it will be revered by all under Heaven—
just as the lowlands gather streams from every direction,
so too its influence is inevitable.

Thus it is called *“the pivot of the world.”*
When the world’s realms converge,
it is because they can descend.
Descending, their *qi* is most *gentle*—
not the utmost *rigidity*.
What is more *vigorous* than the *vigorous* (*yáng*)?
What is more *gentle* than the *receptive* (*yīn*)?
The *vigorous* is *yáng*, the *rigid*;
the *receptive* is *yīn*, the *gentle*.
It is fitting that the *vigorous* (*yáng*) should overcome the *gentle* (*yīn*).
Yet why does the *receptive* often prevail over the *vigorous*?
It is because the *receptive* possesses *stillness*.

The ancients said, *“Stillness governs movement”—*
their words hold no flaw,
just as descent follows ascent—
its force is inevitable.

Much less so for the great realm,
which lowers itself to *nurture* the lesser,
and *virtues* itself to *uplift* others—
could there ever be a realm
that does not come to *revere* or *submit*?

The great realm is the model of *high virtue*,
while *stillness* is the foundation of descent.
From ancient times to now,
the great realm descends to the small realm—
like *Tāng* humbling *Gě Bó*,
ultimately gaining *Gě’s* land,
soothing and possessing it—
or the small realm submits to the great—
like *Gōujī* humbling the *King of Wú*,
eventually gaining *Wú’s* dominion,
encompassing and holding it—
sometimes the great realm does not assert its greatness
but adopts the small realm’s posture,
thus taking the small realm as easily as turning a palm—
sometimes the small realm rests content in its smallness
and serves the great realm,
thus taking the great realm as effortlessly as picking up a blade of grass.

Discussing the mighty realms,
they truly serve as the standard for all nations,
yet in *soothing and guiding* them there is method,
and in *encompassing with kindness* there is strategy.
They do not seek to *annex* all under Heaven,
to unify the mountains and rivers—
rather, they seek to *enfold* the small realms,
making the world one family.
Only those with *great virtue* surpassing others
can achieve such *tranquil inclusiveness*.

It is fitting that the world should converge in *Rén* (*benevolence/heart*),
and all directions submit to *Mìng* (*command/ordain*).
The petty, insignificant realms—
all equal in their *feudal apportionments*,
as *vassal ministers* offering frequent tributes,
rushing forward in fear of falling behind—
they do not desire to *elevate themselves* and *take humiliation*,
nor to *preserve the ancestral temples* and *extend their longevity*—
only to *submit to others* and *ensure their own survival*,
to prolong the *lasting breaths* of the people.
Yet even this requires *great wisdom* surpassing others,
to *restrain themselves* and *descend*—
only then can they be *loved and revered* by the people,
and *Mìng* (*command/ordain*) come to them.

Moreover, humans must have *aspirations* and *desires*—
now the great realm desires to *enfold* others,
the small realm desires to *submit*—
both attain their desires,
one through *Rén* (*benevolence/heart*), one through *wisdom*,
yet neither falls into the *private* pursuits of human desire—
this proves that great and small realms alike
follow their *natural course*,
rest in their *allotted roles*,
and none dare *transgress* their duties.

Though the small realm descends by nature,
its principle is fixed—
the great realm should *especially* descend,
only then does the *single person* stand erect,
and the world find its *reliance*.

The governance of the age is thus—
how much more so in governing one’s body?
*“The great realm”* is an analogy for *original spirit*—
*“descending”* refers to *spirit-light* descending to illuminate the *elixir field*,
while *yīn* essence also descends into the *elixir field*.
When the *Divine Fire* refines,
the essence transforms into *qi*—
this is the *elixir field*, the *original pass*.

The human body’s *total support* (*zǒngchí*),
the *convergence* of the *Five Qi*,
the *condensation* of the *Three Flowers*—
all refine into the *elixir embryo*,
emerge as *spirit* and enter *sainthood*—
none of it occurs without this *single elixir field*.

Thus it is called *“the pivot of the world”*—
like all rivers converging at the sea,
this is where the *elixir* is refined.
Yet the *method of alchemy* values *gentle, yielding essence* as primary,
so it takes its metaphor from the *receptive mother* of the world.

The *receptive mother* is *gentle* and *harmonious*—
this is the *Tàishàng*’s *Dao/Way*,
also called *“concentrating *qi* to achieve *gentleness*”*.
Such *utter gentleness* and *harmony* allow the *original essence*
to dissolve and transform,
giving rise to *qi* and then to *spirit*.

And the *original essence* within,
when *stillness* is held to *nurture* the *kidney-qi*,
until the *Divine Fire* refines,
the essence turns into *qi*—
then the *reverse cultivation* technique is applied,
the *inverted function* performed,
raising and ascending it,
consuming and ingesting it,
returning it to the *earthen cauldron* to *lead govern mercury*,
thus *using the vigorous to govern the receptive*—
this is the work after the *River Vehicle*.

Yet in the *beginning of meditation*,
the *heart* is *external yáng* and *internal yīn*,
while the *kidneys* are *external yīn* and *internal yáng*».

「When considering the post-natal body and its form,
the *external yáng* of the *heart* is the *sacrificial altar* (社),
while the *external yīn* of the *kidneys* is the *receptive* (牝).

Now, when *li* (離) is *empty* (虚) it becomes *yīn*,
and when *kān* (坎) is *full* (满) it becomes *yáng*—
this is what *The Awakening to Reality* (《悟真》) says:
*“Though others are hosts, I am the guest”*;
it is also said:
*“Yáng is the male body, even in women;
yīn is the female body, even in men.”*
This is the *inversion of Heaven and Earth*,
where *li* reverses to become *male* (牡),
and *kān* reverses to become *receptive* (牝).

The method of cultivation demands
that the *heart*’s rigid *qi* be transformed into *gentleness*,
and its restless nature be made *still*;
while the *kidneys*’ *gentle qi* becomes *rigid*,
and its *stillness* turns *active*.

Thus, the *gentle and harmonious* nature of *li*
nurtures the *vigorous and male* essence of *kān*—
this is the saying:
*“Fire nourishes wood’s essence within,
water forges adamantine gold.”*

One must *use the heart to direct the qi*
and *use nature to restrain emotions*.
When emotions do not move recklessly,
it is through *silent stillness* and *gentleness*,
through *humility and forbearance*—
this refines the *heart-nature* (心性).

Therefore, the *sweet nectar* (美液) of the *Upper Field* (上田)
flows into the *Primordial Sea* (元海);
the *essence-liquid* (液) then transforms into *qi*
and enters the *Elixir Field* (丹田).
*“The Great State submits to the Small State”* (大国下小国)
refers to the descent from the *Upper Field* to the *Lower Field* (下田).

*“Taking the Small State”* (取小国)
means extracting the *kidney-yang* (金水) *qi* of the *Elixir Field*,
operating the *River Vehicle* (河车) in reverse,
and ascending it to the *Heavenly Valley* (天谷).

*“The Small State submits to the Great State”* (小国下大国)
refers again to ascending from the *Lower Field* (下田) to *Kūnlún* (昆仑),
then descending into the *Yellow Court* (黄庭).

To *“take the Great State”* (取大国)
is to merge the *golden essence* (金液) of *Kūnlún*
and direct it into the *Yellow Court*.

I use the *sweet nectar* (甘液) of the *Upper Field*
to flow into the *Lower Elixir Field* (下丹田) and generate *qi*,
so when one extracts the *qi* of the *Elixir Field*,
it is the *Great State* descending to take it.
Or, when the *Elixir Field*’s *qi* ascends in reverse to the *Heavenly Valley* (天谷) to generate *essence-liquid*,
then swallowing the *Heavenly Valley*’s *qi*
is the *Small State* descending to take it.

This is the *golden essence* and *kidney-yang* ascending,
*lead-qi* merging with marrow,
*essence* condensing and *qi* harmonizing—
in a moment’s breath, transforming into *sweet dew* (甘露) *divine water* (神水),
flowing to the *upper palate* (上腭),
dropping and returning to its source—
the moment when *essence-liquid* transforms into *qi*.

When the *qi-mechanism* (气机) is fully robust,
once more the *River Vehicle* is operated,
directing it upward to *Kūnlún*,
swallowing the *marrow-essence* (髓精) of the *Brain Sea* (脑海),
and descending it into the *Yellow Court*—
this is the moment when *qi* transforms into *essence-liquid*.

Yet the *Great State*’s *“descending flow”* (下流)
is through *gentleness* and *stillness*,
restful and capacious—
truly possessing *virtue* beyond that of ordinary people,
this is the *spirit* transforming *qi* while *qi* refines *essence*,
filling the *Elixir Field* with abundance.

Thus, there is one who seeks to *accumulate the virtue of others* (畜人之德),
and the *Small State* also has *inner clarity* (内朗) *wisdom* (之智),
knowing its own *power* cannot rival the *Great*—
willingly submitting in homage and obedience,
truly possessing *magnanimity* beyond that of ordinary people.
This is when *essence* generates *qi*, *qi* generates *spirit*,
and all returns in dependence to the *Yellow Court*.

Thus, there is also the *Dao* of *entering to serve others*.
Both seek the same goal without external attachment,
so the *elixir* completes its *nine transformations* (九转),
the *Way* ascends to the *Nine Heavens* (九天),
and one abides eternally with *Heaven and Earth* in shared longevity.

How does their *virtue* intermingle and return?
The supreme secret of refining the body
lies nowhere beyond this—
those who attain it should treasure it,
and not reveal it lightly.

**Chapter Sixty-Two: The Dao as the Most Precious for All Under Heaven**
The *Dao* is the *mystery* of all things,
a treasure for the *virtuous* and a safeguard for the unvirtuous.
*Beautiful speech* can be traded,
*noble conduct* can elevate one’s standing.
Since people are unvirtuous,
why should they be abandoned?

Thus, the *sacrificial altar* (社) and the *three ministers* (三公) are established for the *Son of Heaven*,
though there are *arching walls* to precede the *four steeds* (先驷马),
nothing compares to sitting and advancing this *Dao*.

Why did the ancients hold this *Dao* as most precious?
Is it not to *seek and obtain* it,
to *avoid blame* through its practice?

Thus, it is the most precious for all under Heaven.
The *Great Dao* arises before *Heaven and Earth*,
mingles within *emptiness and non-being*,
faint and obscure—
unseen, unheard, untouched—
yet truly the foundation upon which all things depend for their existence.

*Master Zǐsī* (子思子) said:
*“The *Way* of the *virtuous* is costly yet hidden.”*
Without *Dao*, there is no thing;
without thing, there is no *Dao*.
From the *Great Cycle* (大周) to the *sand boundary* (沙界),
down to the finest *dust-mote* (微尘),
it cannot be sought through *traces or symbols*,
nor exhausted through *words or speech*.
Truly, it contains the *ultimate* without and the *ultimate* with,
the *ultimate* emptiness and the *ultimate* reality—
vast and boundless, profound and unfathomable.
No mystery surpasses this.

The *virtuous* know this *Dao* is the most vital for the human body,
so they cherish and conceal it,
cultivate and treasure it,
never willing to part with it even for a moment.
The unvirtuous also know there is a *Dao*—
practicing it preserves the body and brings *blessings* (福),
while abandoning it shortens life and invites *calamity* (祸).
No better strategy exists for safeguarding the body.

Moreover, when this *Dao* of *Middle Way* (中庸) is expressed in *speech*,
it becomes *beautiful speech*—
like precious goods sold in the marketplace,
all know to love and admire it,
and wish to touch and possess it.
When this *Dao* of *ordinary* (寻常) *Way* is seen in *conduct*,
it becomes *noble conduct*—
like the *status* of a *great lord* or *eminent official*,
all respect and honor it,
and seek to elevate and exalt it.
If it cannot be expressed in *speech*,
then trading in it only invites *humiliation*;
if it cannot be demonstrated in *conduct*,
then offering it only invites *slander*.

The *Classic of Poetry* (《诗》) says:
*“Heaven nurtures the common people,
endowing them with things and principles.
The people’s inherent nature,
loves this *virtue* of *goodness* (懿德).”*
This shows that though *virtue* and *vice* differ,
the heart’s love for *virtue* remains the same.

When I see one who is *virtuous*,
I revere them.
If I see one who is unvirtuous,
why should I despise them?
It is merely the *qi* and *nature* (气质) of their disposition
or the *desires* (物欲) yet unrefined,
that cause them to stray from the *Dao*.
Yet their origin is ultimately no different.

If one can *transform* and *guide* them,
even the most wicked person
may turn toward *virtue*.
Great indeed is the *Dao*’s power—
*Heaven and Earth* abandon no thing,
the *sage* abandons no person.

If one abandons a person,
it is self-abandonment—
how could the *Dao* permit such a thing?

*Heaven* creates the people and establishes their *rulers*,
making them *teachers* as well,
so that they may govern all under Heaven
and place the *three ministers* in order—
this is to *harmonize and guide* the *people*,
to *transform and lead* the *multitudes*.

To *rectify* one’s own body
is to *rectify* the court;
to *rectify* the court
is to *rectify* all under Heaven.»

「Let all nations and regions be in harmony,
and winds shall stir from all directions—
the *Son of Heaven* shall long preserve his reverence,
the *three ministers* shall long enjoy their honors,
and only then shall the task be complete.

If one cannot uphold the *Dao* as *Heaven’s Way*,
to renew and sustain the *people*,
how could one forever preserve *Heaven’s Mandate*,
and enjoy boundless blessings?

Even with the *nobility* of arched walls and treasures arrayed before,
and the *wealth* of four-horse chariots racing behind,
one cannot rest in ease for a moment.

How much better to approach the *Dao* daily and nightly,
ever vigilant, never forgetting,
and thus naturally advance along the *Way*!

The *Chu Book* says:
*"The treasure of Chu is none other than virtue—*
*virtue alone is its treasure."*

The *Shang Book* says:
*"Treasure only the worthy,*
*and the people shall be near and at peace."*

This is the *Dao*—
the most prized by ancient emperors, kings, ministers, and officials alike.

Why did the ancients hold this *Dao* in such esteem?
Because the *Dao* is the inherent *Way* of all people;
seek it, and you shall find it—
its pursuit is swift and effortless.

If one upholds this *Dao*,
they become a true *hero* among mortals;
if one defies this *Dao*,
they become a great *offender* against *Heaven and Earth*.

Is it merely a matter of having faults
and yet failing to avoid the path of depravity?

*Master Zisi* said:
*"The *Dao* must never be abandoned for an instant."*

Let people strive earnestly!
For the *Dao* is a great matter in life—
whether *Son of Heaven*, *three ministers*, or all others,
one must cherish and guard it diligently.

Though one may possess arched walls and four-horse chariots,
it is better to sit and cultivate the *Dao*—
do not claim old age or depleted *qi* as excuses,
for self-deception is no defense.

Know this: even if one borrows *post-heaven* essence, *qi*, and spirit
to forge *golden elixir* and *jade elixir*,
and attain *transcendence* or *sainthood*,
this is but a trifling matter.

The ancients said:
*"The *Dao* is the Great Harmony,"*
and also:
*"The *Dao* is the Void of Non-being."*

Thus, it is clear that those who study the *Dao*
yet fail to grasp the principle of *Void* and *Non-being*,
even if they refine essence and subdue *qi*,
or meditate in *non-duality*,
shall remain no different from the common folk.

Therefore, in cultivating the *Dao* and forging the elixir,
one must take the *Original Spirit* as the master,
the *Original Qi* as the assistant to the spirit,
and *True Breathing* as the means to refine the elixir.

Without the *Original Spirit*,
there is no foundation for the elixir;
without the *Original Qi*,
there is no aid for the elixir.

This is like a womb containing an infant—
without the union of the father’s essence and the mother’s blood,
it remains empty and without substance.

Having obtained the *Original Spirit* and *Original Qi*,
without *True Breathing* to govern them,
the spirit and *qi* cannot coalesce in unity,
merge into one,
and return to the pristine origin of *Great Simplicity*.

I further impart this truth:
When mortals cultivate and refine,
having gained the *Original Spirit* and *Original Qi*,
and mastered *True Breathing*,
they must gather the five into clusters of four,
and merge the three into one—
yet without *True Intent* as their guiding commander,
the *qi* and spirit shall scatter and disperse,
and the elixir shall never form of its own accord.

But whence does *True Intent* arise?
It must emerge from the state of *Void* and *stillness*,
of *ignorance* and *unawareness*—
when suddenly, the *qi*-mechanism is touched,
and awareness begins,
this is the *True Intent*,
not the same as the ordinary mind or intent.

Thus the ancients said:
*"Sainthood is not attained by others—*
*only by those who cultivate this true nature."*

Yet without drawing *qi* from *water* and *essence*,
as resources and assistance,
even the innate true nature shall hang suspended and empty,
and risk falling into the *coarse void*.

Having known the birth of the *golden elixir*,
without *True Breathing* to regulate and nurture it,
how could one gather and refine it into the elixir?

Thus, *True Breathing* is the essential tool for forging the elixir,
and *True Intent* is the sovereign ruler of *True Breathing*.

Those who study the *Dao* yet fail to unite spirit and *qi*,
how could they attain *stillness*?

If one attains the return of spirit and *qi*,
they must ferment and nurture deeply—
only then shall the *golden elixir* be fully realized.

Do not stir the *Bright Awareness* of the ordinary mind,
lest the *golden elixir* and *wood elixir* be separated,
and the *Kan* and *Li* fail to interact.

Through this, I illuminate the mysteries of the *Dao*—
later scholars who gain insight from it
must treasure and guard it carefully!

**Chapter Sixty-Three: The Great as Non-action, the Non-action as Action**

The great is *non-action*,
the *non-action* is action,
the *non-action* is flavorless.

The great and the small,
the many and the few,
repay resentment with *virtue*.

Plan for difficulty in its ease,
and achieve the great in its smallness.

The most difficult matters under *Heaven*
must be done in their simplicity;
the greatest matters under *Heaven*
must be done in their minutiae.

Therefore, the *sage* never strives for the great,
and thus achieves it.

Light promises must be few,
for many shall be untrustworthy;
many undertakings must be few,
for many shall bring difficulty.

Thus the *sage* fears difficulty,
and thus encounters none.

The *Dao* is inherently *Middle Way*—
all may study it, all may attain it.
Yet because of *things* obscuring and *qi* constraining,
without forceful pruning and removal,
how could one perceive the original face?

Like washing clothes: though long stained by dust and filth,
one cannot clean them in a single step—
they must be slowly scrubbed,
gently plucked,
until the old rags are made new again.

If one uses too much force,
not only shall the filth not be removed,
but the clothes may be torn.

Thus, those who seek to penetrate the original truth
must not rush recklessly forward—
at first, they must exert themselves,
but avoid hasty, unmeasured force;
in time, they shall follow the *Middle Way*,
and naturally see the original face.

When their work reaches the stage of refining *Void* into the *Dao*,
they achieve *non-action*;
when they respond to *Nature* without contrivance,
they achieve *actionless action*.
Plain and unremarkable,
what flavor could there be?

Having no flavor,
what satiety could there be?

As for the great returning to the small,
the many yielding to the few,
until the point of retribution—
this is not done through resentment,
but through *virtue*,
all of which are the most wondrous transformations,
the most complete responses to conditions.

Yet in applying this,
there is no partiality—
*virtue* is evenly bestowed;
in repaying resentment with *virtue*,
there is no discordant sentiment—
for *virtue* is the common good of all people,
and repaying with *virtue* is the natural expression of purity.»

「To treat things by returning them to their nature,
and to govern people by aligning with their own *Dao*,
is to respond with greatness and smallness, abundance and scarcity—
all movements follow the natural order of Heaven,
each action is the *Dao*,
everywhere without distinction,
yet never conflicting with oneself,
nor ever clashing with others.

Ah, this is the *Dao* most difficult yet most simple,
most vast yet most minute.

Yet how many practitioners in the world
seek quick results and immediate gains,
often embracing what is difficult,
and favoring what is grand,
without knowing that difficulty arises from simplicity,
and grandeur stems from the minute.

Thus, all great undertakings in the world
must begin with the small.

Since the *Dao* is the root of all things,
how could one not proceed from ease to difficulty,
from minute to vast?

Otherwise, those who advance too swiftly
shall retreat just as quickly—
how then could they hope to reach the realm of divine transformation?

Therefore, the ancient sages knew
that the *Dao* has stages to traverse,
and learning has steps to ascend,
yet they did not ponder grand schemes,
only striving for the immediate essence.
They refined what was coarse,
nurtured the fundamental source,
like water permeating plants—
naturally changing day by day,
transforming month by month,
not seen to grow yet ever growing.

Thus, from the subtle beginnings,
from the crude to the refined,
they moved from *action* and *doing*
to *non-action* and *actionless action*,
ever more plain yet ever more profound,
ever closer yet ever more distant,
until they attained the realm of supreme beauty.

The sage never seeks the grand,
and thus achieves the grand.

Nowadays, scholars at their outset
aspire to become immortals,
the more ambitious their hearts,
the more difficult their tasks—
and so many falter halfway through.

Only through steadfast endurance,
with unwavering resolve,
can the difficult become easy,
the minute remain minute,
and the grand be made small.

I urge scholars to embrace difficulty in simplicity,
to attain grandeur through the minute,
to proceed with measured caution and maturity,
and thus avoid recklessness and superficiality.

Otherwise, not only will they fail to grasp the *Dao*’s profundity,
but they must cultivate sincerity and depth of heart to ever succeed—
for those who treat oaths lightly shall lack trust,
and their regrets shall only deepen;
those who rush to inner cultivation,
favoring ease, shall often face great difficulty,
and retreat shall follow swiftly.

Such is the inevitable course of things.

Thus, the sage’s initial cultivation,
though rooted in ease and the minute,
is marked by ceaseless diligence,
unceasing caution—
for the heart’s work is never truly finished.

Only by first confronting difficulty,
then guiding it like a boat on flowing water,
doing without *doing*,
does one arrive at “no difficulty at all.”

These three lines on *“non-action”*
are the essence of pure, natural effort.
What follows—embracing difficulty in simplicity—
is the intention of seeking profound refinement through gradual approach.

As for the *Dan* method,
when speaking of *lead* and *mercury*,
what are they truly?

Let me clarify:
These substances are none other than the two poles of *yin* and *yang*.
When *mercury* is paired with *lead*,
it is as if *yin* is joined with *yang*—
after their union, primordial *qi* emerges,
then this *qi* is merged with *yin qi* in the central palace,
and thus the *elixir* is formed.

In the *Post-Heaven* realm,
*Li* is the pure *yang* of *Qian* (☰),
*Kan* is the pure *yin* of *Kun* (☷).
With the movement of *qi*,
the *Qian*’s central line enters *Kun*,
and the *Kun*’s central line enters *Qian*’s cavity—
*Qian* then becomes *Void* as *Li*,
and *Kun* becomes *full* as *Kan*.

Thus, though *Qian* is *yang* and contains *yin*,
and *Kun* is *yin* yet holds *yang*,
they are no longer the pristine *yin-yang* of the *Taiji*’s undifferentiated unity.
Yet they remain fundamentally true.

In time, the *spirit* generates *jing*,
and the *qi* transforms into *blood*—
from here, the nature of *qi* and *blood*,
and the destiny of *life-force* (*qi-shù*), emerge.

For those with thinking, perceiving minds,
and bodies of *qi*, *blood*, and form,
they are unlike the original *Qian* and *Kun*.

The adept uses method to draw forth
the *Li*’s single point of *self-mercury* (for *mercury* is the fluid of the heart,
though fluid belongs to *yin*,
it arises from *Li*’s fire and carries its nature),
and sends it down into the *Kan* palace,
to warm the *Kan* palace’s single point of *yin blood* (for *blood* is the water of *Kan*,
though water belongs to *yang*,
it is born from *Kan*’s water and is truly a cold substance)—
as the ancients said:
*“Fire enters the water domain,”*
*“Spirit enters the realm of qi.”*

Just as ice hardens when it meets fire,
or as embers heat a pot,
the *yang qi* naturally warms,
giving rise to a pulsating *yin qi* current.

Although, when fire enters water,
it is like adding embers to a pot’s base,
steaming heat ascends vigorously—
this is the birth of true *lead*.

Through the adept’s *spirit*,
the *yang qi* rises upward to the *nirvana marrow* (for governance alone),
as if baking wine in a heated pot—
the rising vapor is drawn by fire into the celestial vessel,
then condenses as dew dripping into the jar (this is what our teaching calls *“true mercury,”*
and also *“the busy messenger from the Northern Sea’s first tide,
nourishing the ancient tree’s roots in the Eastern Mountain”*—
for it is merely *qi* transformed into fluid).

Then, returning to the furnace for warmth and cultivation,
the fluid again becomes *qi*,
cycling endlessly—
ascending and descending,
until the body’s *qi* and *blood* are exhausted,
the *yin qi* stripped away,
and the mortal form is transmuted into a *golden body*,
the turbid essence into a *Qian* essence,
reverting to the original *Taiji*’s *Void*—
the *Dharma-body* of neither birth nor death.

Jia Yuanxu once said:
*“When speaking of *Kan* and *Li*,
the *lead* and *mercury* within the body,
are both ordinary *lead*—
only when *Kan* and *Li* unite,
do true *yin* and true *yang* converge,
and a single point of true *yang* emerge,
does one attain the primordial true *lead* seed.

Yet without a master’s oral instructions,
even if one forcibly restrains it,
one can only solidify the *color-body* (*sèshēn*),
and when the lower *dantian* is filled and strengthened,
it shall inevitably leak and collapse.

Scholars who attain this *yang* generation
have only completed half the work—
how could they hope to form the embryo and achieve sainthood?

Only by drawing this *yang qi* upward,
merging it with the body’s *yin jing*,
and further combining it with the *spirit marrow* (*shénsuí*)
and *essence fluid* (*língyè*) of the *nirvana marrow* and *vermilion palace*—
this is truly *“the Eastern Neighbor’s daughter (wood-mercury),
and the Western Neighbor’s son (gold-lead),
uniting as husband and wife in the chamber.”*」

The Yellow Crone urges one to drink *gāotú* wine,
and daily to intoxicate oneself with incense and vapor—
this is the union of *Heaven* and *Earth* to forge the elixir,
while previously, only the *Kan-Li* union produced the medicine.

With this true *lead* and true *mercury* united,
one may then refine the *returned elixir*.
*Lead* is the *gold* born from water,
*mercury* is the *wood* born from fire.
Previously, these were but common *lead* and common *mercury*,
but now they are the true *lead* and true *mercury*.

If practitioners follow this method,
cultivating the *spirit* (*shén*) without forcing the *qi*,
they shall not go astray.

**Chapter 64: Non-Doing, Non-Clinging**
The unformed is easy to grasp,
the unmanifest is easy to plan,
the fragile is easy to shatter,
the subtle is easy to disperse.
Act before it arises,
regulate before disorder begins.

A tree thick enough to embrace,
grows from a tiny sprout;
a nine-tiered tower,
begins with a single clod;
a thousand-*li* journey,
starts beneath one’s feet.

The doer brings defeat,
the clinger loses his way.
Thus, the Sage does not act,
so he never fails;
does not cling,
so he never loses.

The people’s undertakings
often falter just as completion nears.
Heed the end as the beginning,
and there shall be no failure.

Therefore, the Sage
wishes yet does not wish,
values not the treasures that are hard to obtain;
learns yet does not learn,
but corrects the errors of others.
He aids the natural unfolding of all things,
yet dares not interfere.

The *Dao* of refining one’s self
begins with restraining desire.
The key to restraining desire:
to regulate it before it arises is easy,
to regulate it as it arises is harder;
to regulate it as it arises is still easier,
but to regulate it once formed is hardest.

Therefore, the *Supreme Dao* says:
*“The unformed is easy to grasp,
the unmanifest is easy to plan.”*
When one dwells in quiet solitude,
the mind is not enslaved by affairs,
affairs do not disturb the mind—
still and unmoving, settled in its place,
one’s grasp of self and preservation of nature
is most effortless.

Moreover, in silence and obscurity,
without knowledge or perception,
no trace or sign to seek,
to then devise plans and ponder—
to dispel idle thoughts and restore sincerity—
its course is supremely smooth,
its opportunity most favorable.

Since the common *qi* is soft and fragile,
and the common mind subtle and fleeting,
before desires become entangled and relentless,
before they twist and turn without end,
to now break these impure thoughts,
to scatter these lustful hearts,
and restore the natural *Way* of Heaven,
the sincere and unerring—
how difficult would it be to sever these karmic ties,
and instantly reveal one’s original nature of *Nirvana*?

This is not another act of doing—
it is merely *“acting before it arises.”*

The ancient sage sought to prevent calamities before their sprouts,
and discerned the opportunities at their nascent stirrings—
thus all smoke and clouds were swept away,
and thorns and brambles never took root.

Again, when the world is at great peace,
and a rogue or petty tyrant seizes the moment to cause strife,
it is no hardship for a lone horseman to emerge,
and instantly witness their surrender—
to govern before chaos arises,
how effortless the method must be!

This work of refining oneself is still easily achieved.
But to perfect the nine transformations,
time cannot be measured in mere years and months.

How many are the common, aimless folk
who fail to grasp the Dao as the grand Way of Heaven and Earth,
and humanity as the true Sage of the cosmos!
Some encounter a dharma assembly by chance
and attain fulfillment in a single lifetime;
others lack the right conditions,
and require countless lifetimes before success.
Some repeatedly cultivate, meet fortunate circumstances,
yet their virtue remains incomplete—
their nature flawed, their disposition perverse—
they nearly attain but then fail,
and fail so utterly that they never succeed.

How profound the mysteries of the Great Dao!
Few truly comprehend its ways.

Let us observe how things come to fruition:
A tree of embrace,
when first born, is but a slender sprout—
through the gentle nurture of yin and yang,
changing daily and monthly,
it grows into a mighty tree.
A nine-tiered tower,
when first raised,
is merely a pile of earth—
through human labor, gathering and refining,
ever new and ever flourishing,
it suddenly becomes a lofty tower.
Or consider the unification of mountains and rivers,
the thousand-li journey to traverse a realm—
can one expect to reach their destination
by merely lifting a foot or counting steps?
No—it begins with one step at a time,
from near to far,
until at last they arrive.

Though called the "Great Dao",
it truly encompasses the vast capacity of Heaven and Earth,
the nurturing power to birth and sustain all things—
how could it not be achieved through laborious layers,
through winding, gradual progress?

Only those who deeply enter the Dao
do not seek swift results,
do not measure gains by proximity.
Though gold and jade may be polished,
their resolve remains unshaken;
though seasons may change,
their diligence knows no variation.
Thus, from small to great,
from low to high,
from near to distant—
like the embrace of a mighty tree,
the rise of a nine-tiered tower,
a thousand-li journey—
they suddenly reveal wonders beyond compare.

Yet, the Dao is the natural Way,
and its practice demands natural effort.
Mencius spoke of *"gathering virtue and generating vital breath"*—
his power lay in *"non-action"* and *"non-forgetting."*
At first, he harmonized with the movement of Heaven and Earth,
and the renewing of creation;
later, he aligned with the ceaseless passage of sun and moon,
yet his radiance remained ever the same.
If one acts *with* intent to act,
then the actor is undone;
if one grasps *with* intent to grasp,
then the grasper is lost.

Heaven and Earth, the sun and moon,
endlessly turning through ages—
do they not achieve transformation without contrivance?

If Heaven and Earth were to act *with* intent to move,
if the sun and moon were to grasp *with* intent to shift,
how could they endure eternally without wear?

The saying goes:
*"If Heaven had emotions, Heaven too would age,
But since the sun has no will, it ever shines bright."*
Is this not the truth?

Thus, the ancient sages
refined the supreme Dao,
marvelously following nature’s course.
They acted without acting—
no failure in their deeds;
they grasped without grasping—
no loss in their virtue.

Yet today’s seekers of the Dao
mistake *non-action* for action,
sometimes practicing, sometimes abandoning—
they do not know when to move or when to rest,
when to align with the natural flow.
Their dynamic and stillness often falter,
far from the ancient path.
Some nearly succeed but then collapse,
and once fallen, never rise again.

The *Book of Documents* says:
*"Be cautious in its end,
for its beginning is all."*
Thus it endures through countless ages without replacement.

As for rare treasures,
all men hold them dear—
the sage blends with the world,
his light undimmed,
yet he seeks the Dao, not wealth.
At first, he does not know
such preciousness exists in human affairs,
so he does not value it—
his detachment is thus clear.

In matters of sight, hearing, speech, and movement,
in daily actions and common affairs—
those who abandon restraint and stray beyond bounds
need not be spoken of.
Even among those who seek the Dao,
some cling to emptiness, some to substance,
some grasp when they should not, some hold back when they should—
all are errors.

Now I alone follow the ancient path,
embrace the old Way,
and express my own views—
not to claim my words are lofty,
but to weigh the Dao’s measure.

I think the Dao is *my* Dao,
learning is *my* learning—
I attain what I attain by myself,
so why speak of learning at all?

Moreover, men often err in excess,
while I alone act without contrivance.
With my Dao of *non-action*,
I mend the errors of others—
this is to rectify myself and thereby rectify others.
And with my Dao of *non-action*,
I aid all things that fall short—
this is to order my own conduct and lead all things—
how dare I act otherwise?

The sage’s body is the Dao’s dwelling,
the people’s and all things’ reliance—
how could I for a moment cease to be?

At the outset, when I spoke of *"its effortless grasp and preservation"*,
those words referred to the single aperture of the Mysterious Pass—
silent and unmoving,
yet responsive and thus harmonious.

Even in the moments of not seeing, not hearing,
this realm holds the true essence—
neither good nor evil.
The Buddha called it *"that"*;
the Confucian sage called it *"the luminous harmony"*—
all speak of the same thing.

---

Like the morning sun upon lotus,
the dawn wind through willows—
tender red and fresh green,
radiant with loveliness.

*The Classic of Changes* says:
*"Heaven and Earth in their primal union,
All things refined in their transformation.
Male and female merge in essence,
All things born from this union."*

It speaks only of the initial *qi* in its gentleness,
still close to Heaven’s origin.

Zhu Xi’s verse declares:
*"A half-acre pond mirrors the sky—
Heaven’s light and clouds drift by."*

This reveals the Dao-heart and human-heart,
distinct yet clear in an instant.

Here, one steadies the will and nurtures the *qi*,
establishes teachings to sever entanglements,
and thus ascends to the other shore.

*The Rites* proclaim:
*"Man is born in stillness—
This is Heaven’s nature."*

When stirred by things, he moves—
This is the nature of desire.

Like Heaven and Earth at the first return of the cycle,
all things revive in spring.

Though things interact and stir desires,
these are still matters of Heaven’s nature,
rooted in emptiness and stillness,
natural and unforced.

Only slight restraint is needed—
no great schemes required—
to curb desire and preserve sincerity,
to quiet evil and return to right.

Like tender shoots and fragile roots,
human desire is easily severed,
while Heaven’s principle may be restored.

The ancients called this the Mysterious Pass’s aperture,
or the Gate of Life and Door of Death.

When the human heart withdraws and hides,
and the Heavenly heart shines forth,
it is because, in the time before disturbance,
one acts and governs.

Yet once the first *yang* stirs,
its mechanism is subtle,
its momentum swift.

By the second and third *yang*,
the spirit condenses, *qi* gathers,
true essence moves on its own—
vast as tides, fluid as melting ice.

All arise from the subtle to the manifest,
from small to great,
from near to far.

To the alchemical stages—
advancing fire, advancing talismans,
the River Vehicle’s transport,
rebirth of the male elixir,
reunion of the female mercury—
boiling, refining, gradually congealing,
spirit complete, *qi* robust,
the pill perfected—
even the six senses tremble,
the six powers fully manifest—
all begin with the Mysterious Pass’s first movement.

At this initial stir,
the water’s source is purest.
As the ancients said:
*"The White Tiger’s first passage—priceless treasure,
The Pool of Flowers—true gold in sacred water."*

If one awakens at this moment and acts,
holding firm, one may then daily circulate one’s own mercury,
enclosing the yin essence—
like the first crescent moon at the third day,
growing to half at the upper arc,
full at the fifteenth.

Thus the sage knows all things under Heaven,
from low to high, near to far,
follow their natural Dao.

To act without acting,
to grasp without grasping—
as Heaven speaks not yet all things move,
how unlike the people’s ruinous deeds,
their failures called success!

This is all from a single piece of pristine clarity,
undivided and whole.

Unknowing what to desire,
one forgets even the thought of desire.
Thus it is said: *"Desire not to desire."*

As for the value of millet and pearls,
there is no striving—
from non-being to being,
yet being remains non-being.
The Daoist’s inherent possession,
needing no external seeking.

Even if one studies,
it is still as if studying nothing.
Thus it is said: *"Study not to study."*

As one’s own purity transforms the world’s杂,
the world’s杂 returns to one’s own purity—
guiding and aiding all things,
rooted in nature alone.
How unlike those who flaunt their private cleverness!

---

**Chapter 65: The Skillful Daoist**

The ancients skilled in the Dao
did not enlighten the people—
they sought to make them simple.

The people’s difficulty in governance
lies in their excess of cleverness.

Thus, ruling with cleverness
is a state’s ruin;
ruling without cleverness
brings the state’s blessing.

Knowing these two principles
is called the Mysterious Virtue.

The Mysterious Virtue is profound,
far-reaching, contrary to things—
only then does one attain Great Harmony.

Under Heaven, all affairs rely on cleverness,
yet the Dao does not rely on cleverness—
it relies on simplicity.
Simplicity is near to the Dao.

The Master’s lineage, passed down,
was grasped by the simpleminded Zengzi.

Thus the ancient sages
governed under Heaven with the Dao.
They did not merely show the people the Dao—
they transformed them into the Dao,
mysterious and indistinct,
all returning to the pure stillness of Heaven—
while the plowman and well-digger
rise with the sun and rest with the moon,
forgetting imperial might in their labor,
following Heaven without knowing it.

Ah! How pure their simplicity!

「From the later generations onward,
scholars and officials no longer valued *qu* (愚) but prized cleverness,
thus giving rise to ever-more intricate schemes,
corrupting the hearts of men,
deepening their avarice and vulgarity daily,
and rendering customs ever more deceitful.

The ruin of these people’s moral standards and rites,
their lawbreaking and transgression of regulations,
their disregard for death—
such cases are countless and difficult to enumerate.

All stem from those who extol talent and favor acute intelligence,
striving to gain falsehood,
while even the simple among the people indulge in guile.
The people’s innate purity has been pierced through,
deceit and cunning abound,
yet in their ceaseless bustle,
one deceives while another fears,
and those in authority find governance beyond their capacity.

Thus it is said:
*"To rule a nation with cleverness is to make it a thief;
to rule without cleverness is to bring it fortune."*

Why is this so?
Because when the people acquire knowledge,
their primordial simplicity is already shattered.
If they remain in ignorance, unaware,
then their original purity endures intact.

These two paths—cleverness and simplicity—diverge,
and their benefits and harms are starkly contrasted.
Rather than value cleverness and invite harm,
why not embrace simplicity and reap its gains?

Understanding these two principles
is not only true for governing the world—
it applies equally to cultivating oneself,
serving as a model to follow.

To grasp this model
is to approach the Dao.

Great cultivators,
even when they see and hear nothing,
return to the state of no thought, no care—
the divine essence of pure stillness.
This cannot be achieved
by merely closing ears and eyes,
or by suppressing acute intelligence,
but only through attaining true equanimity.

If even a single thread of calculation or scheming arises,
the original purity is lost,
and the harmony of simplicity is ruined.

Knowing that cleverness harms oneself,
while simplicity benefits the body,
one should not flaunt their cleverness,
but delight in preserving their simplicity—
this is what is called the *Mysterious Virtue* (玄德).

All that can be named is not the *Mysterious Virtue*;
only that which cannot be named,
profound and boundless,
far-reaching and unfathomable,
can be called the *Mysterious Virtue*.

Though it shares with flying and creeping things,
and with the sluggish and dull,
the quality of having no desires, no knowledge,
yet these creatures cannot grasp the threads of their origins,
living in perpetual darkness and confusion.

Man alone,
from coarse to refined,
from origin to conclusion,
may reach the unity of the Three Primordials (三元),
returning the Great Ultimate (太极) to its original state (归真),
and still attain divine transformation—
how could this not be contrary to things?

In governing a nation, cleverness is not valued,
but in cultivating the Dao, simplicity is all the more precious.
For cleverness is indeed the thief of a nation,
while simplicity is the seed of the Dao.

Can simplicity truly be the seed of the Dao?
Consider the state of *Hun Dun* (混沌),
where there is no thought, no care,
no knowledge—
is this not what is called simplicity?

Suddenly, one awakens—
this is the unborn, unending essence of *I* (我).
None should claim to retain this awakening,
to cultivate the supreme and perfect enlightenment (無上正等正覺),
for only then can one escape the cycle of rebirth,
avoid the forging of yin and yang (陰陽鼓鑄),
and not be ensnared by ghosts and spirits (鬼神拘執).

Even within the *Hun Dun* state,
when one suddenly awakens—
if I guard this true essence without letting it disperse,
this single awakening has already reached *Prajñāpāramitā* (般若波羅蜜).

If one steadfastly upholds and constantly guards it,
the seeds of rebirth will be severed here.

If another thought or perception arises,
it is the post-natal *desire-knowledge* (後天識欲之神) mingling within,
as the saying goes:
*"Countless movements bring forth the root of birth and death,
The foolish call it the original man."* (無量動來生死本，痴人唤作本来人)

In essence,
the divine essence is singular,
but desire makes it dual.

Dual thoughts and triple minds
are the defiled roots and dust—
the cause of birth and death.

Only with one heart,
no dual thoughts,
having right awareness (正念),
and no deluded mind (妄心),
is the Dao found.

If one can dissolve even this single heart and right awareness,
it is the Great Ultimate returning to the Non-Ultimate (太極還於無極),
and the formation of the *Jin Xian* (金仙) lies within this refining of the void (炼虚).

What is *refining of the void* (炼虚)?
It is like the state of *Hun Dun*,
confused and befuddled,
as if in simplicity or drunkenness,
having no knowledge, no awareness—
this is the void.

When seated meditation reaches the stage of no person, no self,
no place, no sky,
this too is refining of the void.

It is also said:
The essentials of learning the Dao
begin with forgetting the self,
proceed to forgetting others,
and end with forgetting the Dao itself—
until one reaches the extreme of forgetting-forgetting,
this is the ultimate attainment.

If one can take this single moment as their master,
and use true awakening as their means,
the Dao is not far.

Yet though the method of refining the void is thus,
its practice must begin with refining the nature (炼性).
The ancients named refining the nature *casting the mirror* (鑄鏡).

If the mind is not refined,
one remains dim and unaware,
even if the truth is right before their eyes—
how much more so for those who possess the Six Perfections (六通)?

If the heart is still clouded by private desires,
it has not yet reached the void.

As in the state after true awakening,
one must not allow even a thread or speck of desire to remain in the chest—
then the *Ling Tai* (靈台) mirror’s treasure
will always shine brightly,
though not necessarily in full attainment,
but in a radiant gleam.

Even within the *Hun Dun* state,
when one suddenly knows—
knowing nothing else—
suddenly awakens—
awakening to nothing more—
this single moment reveals boundless clarity,
illuminating all four directions without obstruction.

However,
a student filled with private desires
cannot suddenly become pure and transparent,
like jade or gold.
How could this be achieved
by a mere moment of emptiness?

One must first forge the *female* and *male blades* (雌雄二劍),
to eliminate both the visible and invisible demons (魔).

If these blades are not sharp,
the demons of desire (欲魔),
form (色魔),
heaven (天魔),
and man (人魔)
cannot be swept away and thoroughly purified,
revealing the true face of the Primordial (乾元).

For human desires and heavenly principles (天理)
have long been entangled;
though one seeks to stand alone in the stream,
the forces opposing them are too great.

Thus, though they know the truth,
they still tread upon it—
for those who lead them into human desires are many,
while those who guide them toward heavenly principles are few.

Now I tell the students:
To perfect the pure *Dharma-body* (法身),
one must first have a pure *divine essence* (神);
To obtain a pure *divine essence*,
one must cultivate boundless *qi* (氣).

What is called *casting the blades* (鑄劍) has no other means—
it is by nurturing the *qi* of the early morning (平旦之氣),
direct and unharmful,
until it becomes vast and robust,
great and firm.»

Once the divine sword is forged and its edge sharp,
it can cleave demons and sever evil.
At that time—
no longer will lewd sounds or ravishing beauty
disturb the mind upon sight,
nor will even shared slumber with a fair woman
rouse awareness;
no longer will malevolent spirits or ominous omens
shake the spirit,
nor will the collapse of Tai Mountain before one’s eyes
inspire fear.

This forging of the divine sword
depends on a will as resolute as the gods—
yet alas, the practice is not deep-rooted,
sometimes pursued, sometimes abandoned,
unwilling to stand firm in the present moment.

If one can sever with a single stroke,
and extinguish private desires the instant they arise,
never allowing them to regenerate—
this is the path to breaking the wheel of birth and death.

The Daoist student has no other secret—
only fear of failing to recognize
the mirror-like divine sword.

If recognized,
the mirror’s light shines universally in this instant,
admitting no evil or delusion,
the wisdom-sword hangs suspended—
desire-demons are instantly severed.
From this moment, with a single thought held firm,
the divine chamber may be perfected,
and the immortal elixir refined.

This mirror-like wisdom-sword
is the essential task of the cultivator.

If the sword’s edge is dull,
how can it sever demonic forces?
Thus, the more one restrains the heart,
the more it grows disordered.

If the precious mirror lacks luminosity,
how can one distinguish principle from desire?
Thus, the more one strives to suppress,
the more they multiply.

Mencius spoke of nurturing *qi* but not of nurturing the heart—
truly, when *qi* is abundant, the heart naturally settles.
Those who merely force the heart,
without knowing that righteousness generates *qi*,
are far from the Dao.

Li Erqu said:
*"The human heart is naturally joyous,
yet private desires bind it.
When desire first stirs,
the true mind becomes aware.
Once aware, it vanishes—
the heart returns to its original joy."*

The humble old man said:
*"Luminous and silent, pervading the sands of the river,
the vulgar and the sage share the same home.
When not a thought arises, the whole body manifests;
the six senses stir—clouds obscure the view.
Severing vexation only deepens affliction,
seeking true suchness is itself delusion.
Worldly affairs follow their course without obstruction,
nirvana and birth-death are but empty flowers."*

Let those who study mind and nature
meditate deeply on these words.

---
**Chapter 66: On the King of All Valleys**

The reason the rivers and seas can be the sovereign of all valleys
